 threatened   of   dire   consequences   (hereinafter   referred   to   as   first statement). It is further the case of the prosecution that under compelling circumstances the prosecutrix made a statement before the Ld.MM in favour of the accused persons. However, immediately after her said statement u/s 164 Cr.PC she went to PS Palam Village to lodge a complaint and explained the reasons for giving the said statement but the police official did not pay any heed. It is alleged that accused have committed offences u/ss. 328/365/366/376/406/506 IPC. 3. During investigation of the present case, the prosecutrix was produced before the Court of Ld. MM for recording of her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC. Her statement was recorded by the Ld. MM on 15.7.2014 (hereinafter referred to as second statement) wherein she has stated that she was running a coaching institute while accused Rajeev (since P.O) was having a mobile shop in Raj Nagar area. She was in need of some experience document as she was intending to enroll for  Ph.D. On the asking of accused Rajeev, she agreed to meet him at Metro Section Sector­9.   He   offered   her   chocolate   consuming   which   she   became unconscious. When she regained consciousness, she found herself in a bus. Accused took her on the point of gun to Katra and committed rape upon her in a hotel. She was kept in the said hotel for four­five days. On State v. Rajeev Verma and others Page 2 of 7 FIR No.334/14, PS Palam Village 30th March he came to Delhi and she was kept her in the house of his Jeeja (i.e accused Nijesh). Co­accused Nijesh and Dinesh committed rape upon her in the said house. The accused took her to Rajasthan, Amritsar and for two months she was raped by them. As regards co­accused Sheela Verma, it is alleged that she took away her gold chain, mangalsutra, ear ring and ring. 4. After   the   investigation   charge­sheet   was   filed     against accused Nijesh and Dinesh for the offences punishable u/s 376/506/34 IPC and against accused Sheela for commission of offences punishable u/ss.323/406/34 IPC. Accused Rajeev Verma is P.O who is alleged to have committed offences punishable u/ss.328/365/366/376/506/34 IPC. 5. I have heard Ms. Satvinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. Dinesh Mudgil, Ld. Counsel for all the accused. 6. Ld.   Counsel   for   the   accused   has   contended   that   the prosecutrix was aged about 27 years at the time of alleged offence while the main accused Rajeev was just 19 years at that time. It is contended that co­accused Rajeev (P.O) was the student of the prosecutrix in her coaching institute. She fell in love with him and it was on her allurement, accused Rajeev accompanied her to various places. Lastly, it is contended that in her first statement u/s 164 Cr.PC, the prosecutrix did not allege State v. Rajeev Verma and others Page 3 of 7 FIR No.334/14, PS Palam Village anything against the accused persons which shows the falsity of the present case.  Ld. Counsel has prayed that there is no sufficient material for framing charge against the accused persons and, therefore, they are liable to be discharged in the present case. 7. On the other hand, Ld. APP for the State has contended that there is sufficient material on record for framing charges against the accused persons. Ld. APP has contended that statement u/s 164 Cr.PC alone should be taken into consideration at the stage of framing charge against the accused persons.  8. I have gone through the case file. The FIR in criminal case is an extremely vital and valuable piece of evidence.FIR No. 160/2014 PS Palam Village U/s 365 IPC was lodged on 29.03.2014 by the husband of the prosecutrix. The prosecutrix was recovered and was produced before Ld. MM for her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC. Her first statement was recorded on 21.05.2014 wherein she did not allege anything against any of the accused persons. She filed a complaint u/s 200 Cr.PC with an application u/s 156 (3) Cr.PC in June 2014 before the Ld.MM. On the directions of the Ld. MM, the present FIR was lodged. The prosecutrix was again produced before the Ld. MM and her second statement dated 15.7.2014 was recorded. State v. Rajeev Verma and others Page 4 of 7 FIR No.334/14, PS Palam Village 9. In her first statement, the prosecutrix 'X' did not make any allegation of rape against accused Rajeev, Nijesh and Dinesh.  It was only in the second statement u/s 164 Cr.PC, allegation of rape were made. There is delay in lodging the FIR which has not been adequately explained. 10. At the time of hearing of bail application of accused Dinesh Dhaka, it was admitted by the IO that as per call detail record and location chart of the mobile phone of accused Dinesh, during the time when the alleged offence is stated to have been committed, he was nowhere near the place where the prosecutrix claims to have been subjected to sexual assault. 11. The prosecutrix has made vague averments in the FIR as well as in her second statement u/s 164 Cr.PC from which it is very difficult to ascertain when and in what manner she was abducted and subjected to rape. 12. Prosecutrix 'X' was medically examined at DDU Hospital, New Delhi on 24.07.2014 and the MLC placed on record does not reveal any fresh sexual assault upon her.   13. Though not referred to or relied upon,  it has been observed by Madhya Pradesh High Court in judgment – Sunder Singh v. State of State v. Rajeev Verma and others Page 5 of 7 FIR No.334/14, PS Palam Village M.P., Cr.R No.607/2013 decided on 3.9.2013 as under :   “42. The prosecution, having regard to the right of an accused to have a fair investigation, fair inquiry and fair trial as adumbrated under Article 21 of the Constitution of India, cannot at any stage be deprived of taking advantage of the materials which the prosecution itself have placed on record. If upon perusal of the entire materials on record, the court arrives at an opinion that two views are possible, charges can be framed, but if only one and one view is possible to be taken favouring the accused, the court shall not put the accused to harassment by asking him to face a trial. Please see: State of Maharashtra v. Som Nath (1996) 4 SCC 659. In the case at hand, if the Court allowed to asking applicant face the trial on above discussed evidence, definitely it will amount to put the applicant for harassment.”  14. After examining the documentary as well as oral evidence which the prosecution proposes to adduce to prove the guilt of the accused, even if fully accepted, before it is challenged by cross­ examination or rebutted by defence evidence, if any, is not showing that accused­Nijesh and Dinesh committed the alleged offence u/s 376 IPC for which they are being prosecuted. 15. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, after sifting and weighing the evidence for the limited purpose of finding out whether or not a prima facie case is made out against the accused, I am of the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against accused Dinesh and Nijesh for framing a charge for committing offence punishable under Sections 376 IPC. Accordingly, State v. Rajeev Verma and others Page 6 of 7 FIR No.334/14, PS Palam Village accused Dinesh and Nijesh in the present case are discharged for the commission of the offence punishable u/ss. 376 IPC. Other offences are triable are the court of Ld. M.M.  The accused are directed to appear before the Court of concerned Ld.MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi at 3 p.m today itself who shall proceed further in the matter in accordance with law. Vide  order dated 12.04.2017, the charges were framed against the accused for the commission of offences u/s.376/506 IPC to which he pleaded not guilty and claimed trial. 5. I have heard Ms. Satvinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. Jai Dev Sharma, Ld. Counsel for the accused. I have also perused the entire material on record. 6. Prosecution in support of its case has examined the prosecutrix as PW1.  She has deposed that in the month of December, 2016 she was residing in Uttam Nagar (address withheld) with her husband and children. She was associated with an NGO. One day in December, 2016 she received phone calls from mobile phone of the accused. She told him not to contact her again as she was already married. However, even thereafter, the accused used to send SMS on her mobile phone. She has further deposed that on 19.12.2016 when she was going to Sarvodya Kanya Vidhalaya from her house, accused waylaid her. He requested her to accompany him to his house to which she agreed. On reaching his house, accused demanded Rs.10,000/­ from her as loan. She told him that she would give him money after SC No.196/17 (State vs. Anindhya Kumar)                                     Page 2 of  4        (FIR No.03/17, P.S. Bindapur)                                           consultation   with   her   husband.   Thereafter,   the   accused   started continuously called her on her mobile phone demanding Rs.10,000/­ from her. Even after the accused was informed that she was unable to advance loan, he continued calling her regularly. She has deposed that as she was disturbed by the accused, she discussed the matter with advocates an relatives who advised her to lodge a complaint against the accused. She has further deposed that on 01.01.2017 she had consumed sleeping pills and was taken to hospital by her husband.  On 02.01.2017 she made a statement to the police that she had consumed sleeping   pills   as   she   was   under   depression   and   nobody   was responsible for the same. She has proved her said statement as Ex.PW1/A.   She   has   further   deposed   that   on   03.01.2017   under misguidance of some of her friends, she made a complaint Ex.PW1/B to the police. However, she had not gone through the contents of the same. Same is her stand for her statement u/s.164 Cr.PC Ex.PW1/C that it was given under misguidance of her friends and relatives. As per PW1, on 20.2.2017, she handed over her medical papers to the IO which were seized vide memo Ex.PW1/D. 7. Prosecutrix was declared hostile and was allowed to be cross   examined   by   the   Ld.   APP.   However,   even   after   cross­ examination nothing incriminating has come out in evidence against the accused. Prosecutrix has categorically denied the suggestion that the complaint­Ex.PW1/A and her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC­Ex.PW1/B being made voluntarily by her. She further denied the suggestion that SC No.196/17 (State vs. Anindhya Kumar)                                     Page 3 of  4        (FIR No.03/17, P.S. Bindapur)                                           she has given a false statement in the court being won over by the accused. 8. From the testimony of PW1 i.e. prosecutrix, it is clear that prosecutrix was neither raped nor threatened by the accused at any point of time.  As the prosecutrix has not supported the case of the prosecution, the examination of other witnesses was dispensed with. 9. The statement of the accused u/s.313 Cr.PC was also not recorded as there is no incriminating evidence against them. 10. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, I am of the opinion that the prosecution has failed to prove its case against the accused. Hence, accused in the present case is acquitted. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged. Documents, if any, be returned to the surety. In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., the accused is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance   before   the   High   Court   of   Delhi   in   the   event   the prosecution wishes to file an appeal challenging the present judgment. From the testimony of PW1 i.e. prosecutrix, it is clear that prosecutrix was never raped by the accused at any point of time.  As the prosecutrix has not supported the case of the prosecution, the examination of other witnesses was dispensed with. 10. Accused is facing trial on allegations of hurting, threatening, confining & committing rape on  prosecutrix  aged about 29 years as well as for destruction of evidence.  2.  FIR in question was registered on complaint dated 14.11.2016 lodged by prosecutrix alleging that she is acquainted with accused Kundan Singh Negi for last two months. In his house accused gave beating to her, destroyed her mobile and forcibly committed rape upon her at 11 PM. In the morning under threat accused administered I-pill to her. Then accused let prosecutrix go to her house. On 12.11.2016, at about 3 AM accused again started threatening her to make her nude video viral and also tried to inform her family members. Under threat of accused, on 13.11.2016 prosecutrix went to his house to Judgment 2 of 27  SC No: 168/17 State Vs. In the meantime, family members of prosecutrix called and prosecutrix told them that accused has forcibly confined her. As a result her family members made a complaint in nearby police station. SI Dhir Singh of that Police Station called accused, only thereafter accused allowed prosecutrix to go home. Kundan Singh Negi 14.  As far as the argument that the FIR does not give entire details of the incident is concerned, it has to be kept in mind that it is settled law that FIR is not an encyclopedia of facts and it is not expected from a victim to give details of the incident either in the FIR or in the brief history given to the Doctors. FIR is not an encyclopaedia which is expected to contain all the details of the prosecution case; it may be sufficient if the broad facts of the prosecution case alone appear.  15. In present case, as we notice, prosecutrix gave description of the incident of 10.11.2016 by narrating that accused under threat to make her video viral raped her and broke her mobile. If we compare her testimony recorded in Court vis-a-vis her complaint we would find that prosecutrix narrated the incident of 10.11.2016 in graphic detail. In her testimony prosecutrix explains her plight and the sequence of events which unfolded on   the   night   of   10.11.2016.   Her   deposition   is   not   an improvement of her complaint but detailing of the events.    Judgment 16 of 27  SC No: 168/17 State Vs. Kundan Singh Negi 16. Prosecutrix in her statement  Ex PW1/D  (recorded U/s 164 Cr.P.C) as well shared details of both the incidents dated 10.11.2016 & 13.11.2016 but in her testimony she went into the minute details which certainly cannot be termed as material improvement but only explanatory in nature. 17. Prosecutrix explains that she was not able to comprehend the behavior of accused on the night of 10.11.2016 when accused forcibly removed her clothes and threw her before his friends as if they could use her for their pleasure. Prosecutrix wanted to know the reason behind it.  Her explanation appears to be truthful. A person in intimate relationship with other is not expecting such an inhuman behavior from his/her partner and in order to find an answer to her ordeal prosecutrix might have wanted to have an explanation from accused. 22.As far as testimony of prosecutrix that she was in consensual physical relationship is concerned, her admission in this regard gives   strength   to  case   of  prosecution  that   testimony   of prosecutrix is truthful and reliable.    23. Prosecutrix did not conceal anything about her relationship with accused. She admits her physical relations with him and Judgment 20 of 27  SC No: 168/17 State Vs. Kundan Singh Negi the fact that even after lodging of FIR she went to meet accused in jail and even stayed with him. Fact that prosecutrix met accused in jail after lodging of FIR or stayed with him does not absolve accused from what accused did to prosecutrix between 10.11.2016 to 13.11.2016. 24. Delay in lodging of FIR: Ld defense Counsel submits that FIR in question was registered after three days of alleged incident of rape and there is no explanation by prosecutrix as to why she didn't report the incident of rape on 10.11.2016 itself.  29.While appreciating the question as to why the FIR was not registered by prosecutrix at once it has to be kept in mind that different people /witnesses react differently in differently situations, whereas some become speechless while some other Judgment 23 of 27  SC No: 168/17 State Vs. Kundan Singh Negi run away from the scene and yet there are some, who may come forwarded with courage, conviction and belief that the wrong should be remedied. As a matter of fact, it depends upon individuals and individuals. There cannot be any set pattern or uniform rule of human reaction. Mere delay in lodging of the report  may not by itself be fatal to the case of prosecution but delay has to be considered in background of facts and circumstances in each case and is a matter of appreciation of evidence by Court of fact. 30.Testimony   of   prosecutrix   shows   that   after   incident   of 10.11.2016, she again went to house of accused on 13.11.2016 to end her relationship with him and to request him to delete her video (video Ex P-1 extracted from mobile of accused in which prosecutrix is seen nude). On 13.11.2016, accused again assaulted prosecutrix and confined her. So much so, accused removed her T-Shirt and bra and threatened that she would have to establish physical relations with his friends who were  Judgment 24 of 27  SC No: 168/17 State Vs. Kundan Singh Negi sitting outside. Accused then after opening the door,  made her visible to his friends. Prosecutrix cried and bowed her head on the feet of accused but accused told her to get aside otherwise he would kick her. When friend of accused came there accused then told his friend to see prosecutrix properly. Not only this accused did not let prosecutrix to go.  31.Events as it happened indicate that even after the incident of 10.11.2016 prosecutrix might have not reported the matter to police but cruel behavior of accused with her on 13.11.2016 fueled her emotion and made her to report the incident. Testimony of PW7 (brother of prosecutrix) and PW13 SI Dhir Singh demonstrates that accused confined prosecutrix and only let her go, when PW13 called accused after brother of prosecutrix made a complaint to police.  Judgment 25 of 27  SC No: 168/17 State Vs. Kundan Singh Negi 32.Thus, in the light of above noted circumstances delay in lodging of FIR does not affect the truthfulness of version of prosecutrix nor the prosecution story. 33. From above stated discussions it emerges: i) Testimony of prosecutrix is trustworthy and reliable. ii) On 10.11.2016 Prosecutrix was raped, abused and physically   assaulted   by   accused.   Accused   hurt prosecutrix and threatened her that he will show her nude video to her family & friends. iii)   On   13.11.2016,   accused   confined   &   abused prosecutrix. Accused even offered prosecutrix to his friends.  iv)   Nude   video   (Ex.P-1)   of   prosecutrix   stands recovered and proved.   v) Medical evidence supports prosecution story. vi)  However, there is no evidence on record that accused is guilty of destruction of any evidence. Circumstances indicate that accused broke mobile out of anger and not with a view cause disappearance of evidence. Nonetheless, nude video stands recovered. Judgment 26 of 27  SC No: 168/17 State Vs. Kundan Singh Negi 34. CCoonncclluussiioonn:: Testimony of prosecutrix is found trustworthy and reliable in respect of incident of sexual & physical assault, threatening as well as confinement by accused. Allegations found corroboration from medical evidence and testimony of other   prosecution   witnesses.  Accordingly,   accused   stands convicted   for   offences   punishable   Under   Section 323/376/506/342   IPC.   Accused   is   not   found   guilty   of destruction of any evidence. Hence, stands acquitted for offence punishable U/s 201 IPC. Matter be listed for hearing arguments on quantum of sentence for 26.09.2017. (GAUTAM MANAN)                                ASJ (SFTC) /SOUTH WEST                                                                   DWARKA COURTS:DELHI     Judgment 27 of 27

 recorded. After completion of investigation, the charge­sheet was filed against   the   accused   for   the   commission   of   offences   punishable u/s.376/323/506 IPC. 3. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for State and Sh. Ravinder Kumar, Ld. Counsel for the accused. Ld. Counsel for the accused has contended that the accused has been falsely implicated in this case by the prosecutrix to extort money. According to him, there is no sufficient evidence on record to frame charges against the accused. 4. On the other hand, Ld. APP for State has contended that there is sufficient material for framing charges against the accused. 5. I have gone through the file. There is delay in lodging the FIR which has not been adequately explained. No specific dates and time of alleged offences have been mentioned by the prosecutrix in her complaint to the police on which present FIR was registered. The prosecutrix did not undergo her internal medical examination when she was taken to the hospital on 02.9.2016. She did not support the prosecution in her statement u/s.164 Cr.PC which was recorded on 02.9.2016. She has categorically stated in her said statement that she was not raped by the accused. It is the settled law that the statement recorded u/s.164 Cr.PC is on a higher pedestal than the statement u/s.161 Cr.PC. State v. Kishan.                                                                                                                      Page 2  of 4 ((FIR No. 249/16, PS Baba Haridas Nagar) The statement u/s.161 Cr.PC dated 09.9.2016 is of no consequence after the statement on oath of the prosecutrix u/s.164 Cr.PC. 6. The prosecutrix was taken to the hospital and in the presence of her husband, she refused to undergo her internal medical examination. The MLC bears the signature of her husband also. On the said MLC, the doctor has opined ­ “since assault was 10 yrs. ago medical examination not required”. 7. It is the settled law that order framing the charges does substantially affect the persons and the Court must not automatically frame the charge merely because the prosecution authorities, by relying on the documents referred to in Section 173 Cr.PC, consider it proper to institute the case.  8. Though not referred to or relied upon,  it has been observed by Madhya Pradesh High Court in judgment – Sunder Singh v. State of M.P., Cr.R No.607/2013 decided on 3.9.2013 as under :   “42. The prosecution, having regard to the right of an accused to have a fair investigation, fair inquiry and fair trial as adumbrated under Article 21 of the Constitution of India, cannot at any stage be deprived of taking advantage of the materials which the prosecution itself have placed on record. If upon perusal of the entire materials on record, the court arrives at an opinion that two views are possible, charges can be framed, but if only one and one view is possible to be taken favouring the accused, the court shall not put the accused to harassment by asking him to face a trial. State v. Kishan.                                                                                                                      Page 3  of 4 ((FIR No. 249/16, PS Baba Haridas Nagar) Please see: State of Maharashtra v. Som Nath (1996) 4 SCC 659. In the case at hand, if the Court allowed to asking applicant face the trial on above discussed evidence, definitely it will amount to put the applicant for harassment.”  9. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, after sifting and weighing the evidence for the limited purpose of finding out whether or not a prima facie case is made out against the accused, I am of the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against the  accused for framing a charge against him for committing   offences   punishable   under   Sections   376/323/506   IPC. Accordingly, the accused in the present case is discharged. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged. In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., accused is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to challenge the present order by filing the appropriate petition in the High Court. Ahlmad is directed to page and bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record. File be consigned to Record Room.  DDU Hospital on 17.9.2016. Her statement u/s.164 Cr.PC was got recorded on 19.9.2016. The accused was arrested. Statements of the witnesses were recorded and after completing the investigation, the chargesheet was filed in the court. 3. After supplying copies of documents u/s. 207 Cr.PC, Ld. M.M. committed the present case to the Court of Sessions. 4. Vide  order dated 07.3.2017, charge u/s.376 IPC against accused was framed. 5. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. Vinod Pant, Ld. Counsel for the accused. I have also perused the entire material on record. 6. Prosecution   in   support   of   its   case   has   examined   the prosecutrix as PW1. She has deposed that accused is known to her for the last about one year. They became acquainted with each other while working in a restaurant at Dwarka (name of the restaurant is with held). They   started   liking   each   other.   She   has   further   deposed   that   on 15.09.2016 at about 3­4 pm, she voluntarily accompanied the accused to the house of his  Jija  at Moti Nagar and they had consensual sexual relations with him.  She tried to call the accused for two days. He did not answer her calls whereupon she got scared and in a fit of anger lodged complaint­ Ex.PW1/A with the police. Same is her stand regarding her State v.  Lokesh Chand. Page 2 of 4 (FIR No.343/16, PS Chhawla)  statement under section 164 Cr. P.C. (Ex. PW1/B). As per PW1, on 02.10.2016 she married the accused at Arya Samaj Mandir, Delhi.  She has proved the certificate of marriage in this regard as Ex. PW1/C.  7. Prosecutrix was declared hostile and was allowed to be cross examined by the Ld. APP. However, even after her cross­examination nothing incriminating has come out in evidence against the accused.  8. From the testimony of PW1 i.e. prosecutrix, it is clear that accused never committed rape upon the prosecutrix and the physical relations between them were consensual in nature.  As the prosecutrix has not supported the case of the prosecution, the examination of other witnesses was dispensed with. 9. The statement of the accused u/s.313 Cr.PC has also not been recorded as there is no incriminating evidence against him. 10. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, I am of the opinion that the prosecution has failed to prove its case against the accused. Hence, accused in the present case is acquitted. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged.   Documents, if any, be returned to the surety. In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., accused is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to file State v.  Lokesh Chand. Page 3 of 4 (FIR No.343/16, PS Chhawla)  an appeal challenging the present judgment.  Ahlmad is directed to page and bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record. State v.  Lokesh Chand. Page 4 of 4 (FIR No.343/16, PS Chhawla) 

 DDU Hospital, Hari Nagar, New Delhi on 27.10.2016. Her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC was recorded by Ld. MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi on 28.10.2016. The statements of witnesses conversant with the facts were recorded. After completion of investigation, a charge­sheet was filed against the accused for commission of offence under Section 376 IPC.  4. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. Chander Prakash Sharma, Ld. Counsel for the accused. 5. Ld. Counsel for the accused has contended that accused has been falsely implicated in this case. According to him, no prima facie case for the alleged offence is made out against the accused and he is liable to be discharged.  6. On the other hand, Ld. APP for the State has contended that there is sufficient material on record for framing charge against the accused.  7 I have gone through the case file. The FIR in criminal case is an extremely vital and valuable piece of evidence for the purpose of corroborating the oral evidence adduced at the trial. It is well settled proposition of law that a mere delay itself cannot be a ground to disbelieve the entire case of the prosecution. The effect of delay is to be understood in the light of the plausibility of the explanation forthcoming State v. Nigam Force Page 2 of 5 (FIR No.774/16 PS Uttam Nagar) and must depend for consideration on all the facts and circumstances of a given case. Though not referred to or relied upon, in case of Dilawar v. State of Delhi, 2007 Cri.LJ 4709,  it has been held by the Apex Court that in criminal trial one of the cardinal principles for the Court is to look for plausible   explanation   for   the   delay   in   lodging   the   report.   Delay sometimes affords opportunity to the complainant to make deliberation upon   the   complaint   and   to   make   embellishment   or   even   make fabrications. 8. The delay of one or two days in lodging the FIR may be bonafide, reasonable and justified in the facts and circumstances of a given case. However, in the present case there is inordinate delay in lodging the FIR.  9. In her complaint on which present FIR was lodged it is alleged that accused committed rape upon the prosecutrix in August and September 2016. However, she has not supported the prosecution in her statement u/s.164 Cr.PC which was recorded on 28.10.2016. She has categorically   stated   in   her   said   statement   that   accused   established physical relations with her consent. It is the settled law that the statement recorded u/s.164 Cr.PC is on a higher pedestal than her other statements recorded before the police. Even in her subsequent statement u/s 161 State v. Nigam Force Page 3 of 5 (FIR No.774/16 PS Uttam Nagar) Cr.PC dated 28.10.2016, she has not supported the prosecution case. Her husband   in   his   statement   u/s.161   Cr.PC   dated   28.10.2016   has corroborated the version of the prosecutrix. The medical evidence against the accused is zero. 10. It is the settled law that order framing the charges does substantially affect the persons and the Court must not automatically frame the charge merely because the prosecution authorities, by relying on the documents referred to in Section 173 Cr.PC, consider it proper to institute the case. 11. Though not referred to or relied upon,  it has been observed by Madhya Pradesh High Court in judgment – Sunder Singh v. State of M.P., Cr.R No.607/2013 decided on 3.9.2013 as under :   “42. The prosecution, having regard to the right of an accused to have a fair investigation, fair inquiry and fair trial as adumbrated under Article 21 of the Constitution of India, cannot at any stage be deprived of taking advantage of the materials which the prosecution itself have placed on record. If upon perusal of the entire materials on record, the court arrives at an opinion that two views are possible, charges can be framed, but if only one and one view is possible to be taken favouring the accused, the court shall not put the accused to harassment by asking him to face a trial. Please see: State of Maharashtra v. Som Nath (1996) 4 SCC 659. In the case at hand, if the Court allowed to asking applicant face the trial on above discussed evidence, definitely it will amount to put the applicant for harassment.”  12. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, after State v. Nigam Force Page 4 of 5 (FIR No.774/16 PS Uttam Nagar) sifting and weighing the evidence for the limited purpose of finding out whether or not a prima facie case is made out against the accused, I am of the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against the  accused for framing a charge against him for committing offences punishable under Section 376 IPC. Accordingly, the accused in the present case is discharged. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged. In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., accused is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to challenge the present order by filing the appropriate petition in the High Court. Ahlmad is directed to page and bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record. File be consigned to Record Room.   State vs. Pradeep Kumar Sethi The copy of charge sheet was supplied to the accused under section 207 Cr.P.C and on 15.12.2017, charge under section 366 IPC and Section 6 r/w Section 5 (l) of POCSO Act was framed upon the accused. The accused pleaded not guilty and claimed trial. 3. The prosecution in order to prove the charge against the accused examined two witnesses. Child victim was examined as PW-1 and father of child victim was examined as PW-2. 4. The prosecution relied upon following documents: (i)     Statement u/s 164 Cr.P.C. of child victim  Ex.PW-1/A (ii)    MLC of child victim  Ex.PW-1/B (iii)   Complaint/statement of father of child victim Ex.PW-2/A          to the police 5. Arguments heard. Record perused and considered. 6. PW-1, child victim deposed that on 25.12.2016 she went with her friends to celebrate Christmas Day but after celebrating Christmas when she was going to meet her other friend she lost the way and moved here and there for 3-4 days. PW-1 further deposed that on 02.01.2017, she met accused, who took her to his house and informed her parents, who came to the house of the accused to take her. PW-1 did not support the case of the prosecution and turned FIR No. 891/2016     PS: Uttam Nagar 2  of  3  State vs. Pradeep Kumar Sethi hostile, therefore, Ld. Addl. PP cross examined her after seeking permission from the court. However, nothing material came in the cross-examination of PW-1.  PW-1 denied the suggestion that the accused had taken her to his house and made physical relation with her. PW-2, father of child victim did not support the case of prosecution by deposing that he had only made missing complaint to the police about the child victim and after 2-3 days, she came back to her home on her own. PW-2 was cross examined by Ld. Addl. PP after seeking permission from the court. However, nothing material came in the cross-examination of PW-2. The FSL result has also not supported the case of the prosecution. The FSL result is Mark A (marked today, while passing this order/judgment). Hence, from the deposition of PW-1 and PW-2 nothing incriminating came against the accused and the prosecution has failed to prove its case. 7. As there was no incriminating evidence against the accused, therefore, statement of accused u/s 313 Cr.P.C. was dispensed with. The accused Pradeep Kumar Sethi @ Ruddu is acquitted from the charge of offence 6 r/w 5 (l) of POCSO Act and section 366 IPC. The bonds of accused and his surety under section 437 A Cr.P.C. are accepted.  relations with him. On the basis of the above complaint, FIR under Sections 376 IPC and 4 POCSO Act was registered. The accused was apprehended and produced before the Juvenile Justice Board. The statements of the witnesses under Section 161 Cr.P.C. were recorded.  2. All the accused appeared before the trial court and were admitted to bail on 4.1.2016. 3. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. R K Rawat, Ld. Counsel for all the accused. I have gone through the file. 6. Ld. Counsel for the accused has contended that accused have State v. Jitender Kumar Batra and others Page 2 of 5 (FIR No.1322/15 PS Bindapur) been falsely implicated in this case. According to him, accused Krishna Batra is/was the landlady of the premises where the prosecutrix 'X' was residing as a tenant. A civil case is also pending between the parties.  Ld. Counsel has prayed that all the accused be discharged in this case.  7. On the other hand, Ld. APP for the State has contended that there is sufficient material on record for framing charges against the accused. 8. I have gone through the case file. In her complaint dated 12.9.2015 which is a handwritten complaint of the prosecutrix, there are no allegations of attempt to rape. Prosecutrix was taken for her medical examination to DDU Hospital on 12.9.2015 itself. She did not mention at that time that an attempt to rape was made upon her by accused Jitender Batra. In her statements u/s 161 Cr.PC dated 12.9.2015 and 24.9.2015 and also in statement of Neeraj u/s 161 Cr.PC dated 26.11.2015, no allegations   of   attempt   to   rape   are   levelled.   The   said   Neeraj   had accompanied the prosecutrix to the spot of incident. The allegations of attempt to rape were made by the prosecutrix in her complaint to the CP in December 2015 and before Ld. MM on 18.1.2016. In her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC, it is alleged by the prosecutrix that a complaint was made against the accused by her on 20.8.2015. However, there is nothing on State v. Jitender Kumar Batra and others Page 3 of 5 (FIR No.1322/15 PS Bindapur) record that any such complaint was made by her. 9. After the allegations of attempt to rape were made by the prosecutrix, statement of Neeraj u/s 161 Cr.PC was recorded by the Police on 19.8.2016. In his said statement, Neeraj has categorically stated that the prosecutrix did not tell him about rape, theft, eve­teasing or beatings by the accused persons. 10. The medical evidence against the accused persons is zero. There is delay in levelling the allegations of attempt to rape by the prosecutrix which has not been adequately explained. Even independent witness Neeraj has not supported the prosecution with regard to rape. In the facts and circumstances of this case, the statement of the prosecutrix u/s 164 Cr.PC cannot be treated as a gospel truth to frame charges against the accused persons for the offence u/s 376/511 IPC.  11. Though not referred to or relied upon, it has been observed by the Apex Court in judgment –  Union of India v. Prafulla Kumar Samal, (1979) 3 SCC 4, that the Court has power to sift and weigh the evidence – although for the limited purpose of finding out whether a prima facie case against the accused has been made out or not. It has also been held that where materials placed before the Court disclose grave suspicion against the accused, the Court would be fully justified in State v. Jitender Kumar Batra and others Page 4 of 5 (FIR No.1322/15 PS Bindapur) framing a charge and proceeding with the trial. By and large, however, if two views are equally possible and the judge is satisfied that the evidence produced before him gives rise to some suspicion, but not grave suspicion against the accused, he will be fully within his right to  discharge the accused.  12. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, I am of the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against all the accused for framing charge against them for   committing   offence   punishable   under   Section   376/511/34   IPC. Accordingly, all the accused in the present case are discharged for the offence punishable u/s. 376/511/34 IPC only. Other offences are triable by the Court of Ld.MM. Accused are directed to appear before the Court of concerned Ld.MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi 14.3.2017.  Ld. MM shall proceed further in the matter in accordance with law. Dictated & announced today in                 (PRAVEEN KUMAR) open court on 08.03.2017.  Addl. Sessions Judge (SFTC)                                 Dwarka Courts, New Delhi. State v. Jitender Kumar Batra and others Page 5 of 5 (FIR No.1322/15 PS Bindapur)

 3. During investigation prosecutrix was medically examined at DDU Hospital, Hari Nagar, New Delhi on 15.12.2015.  Her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC was recorded by Ld. MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi on 17.12.2015. The statements of witnesses conversant with the facts were recorded. After completion of investigation, a charge­sheet was filed against   the   accused   for   commission   of   offences   under   Sections 376/323/427/506/511 IPC.  4. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. Jai Dev Sharma, Ld. Counsel for the accused. 5. Ld. Counsel for the accused has contended that accused has been falsely implicated in this case. There is delay in lodging the FIR which has not been adequately explained. According to him, no prima facie case for the alleged offences is made out against the accused and he is liable to be discharged.  6. On the other hand, Ld. APP for the State has contended that there is sufficient material on record for framing charges against the accused. 7. I have gone through the case file. The FIR in criminal case is an extremely vital and valuable piece of evidence for the purpose of corroborating the oral evidence adduced at the trial. It is well settled State v. Himanshu Kargeti Page 2 of 6 (FIR No.1586/15 PS Uttam Nagar) proposition of law that a mere delay itself cannot be a ground to disbelieve the entire case of the prosecution. The effect of delay is to be understood in the light of the plausibility of the explanation forthcoming and must depend for consideration on all the facts and circumstances of a given case. Though not referred to or relied upon, in case of Dilawar v. State of Delhi, 2007 Cri.LJ 4709,  it has been held by the Apex Court that in criminal trial one of the cardinal principles for the Court is to look for plausible   explanation   for   the   delay   in   lodging   the   report.   Delay sometimes affords opportunity to the complainant to make deliberation upon   the   complaint   and   to   make   embellishment   or   even   make fabrications. 8. The delay of one or two days in lodging the FIR may be bonafide, reasonable and justified in the facts and circumstances of a given case. However, in the present case there is inordinate delay in lodging the FIR.  9. In her complaint on which present FIR was lodged it is alleged that one day accused sexually harassed her. However, no date and time have been specified in her said complaint. The FIR was lodged for the offence u/s 376 IPC. In her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC the prosecutrix has alleged that in the starting of the month of September 2015, accused State v. Himanshu Kargeti Page 3 of 6 (FIR No.1586/15 PS Uttam Nagar) attempted to commit rape upon her. On the said statement of the prosecutrix, after investigation charge sheet was filed for the commission of offences punishable u/s 376/511 IPC.  Thus, the prosecutrix has made improvements in her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC. Even in her statement u/s 164 Cr.P.C., she has not mentioned exact date and time of alleged offence. 10. The accused and the prosecutrix were acquainted with each other.  The accused was granted anticipatory bail by the High Court of Delhi. While granting anticipatory bail to the accused, the High Court observed as under : “As per the FIR, the allegations against the petitioner are that he harassed/raped the complainant in his house three months prior to the written complaint given by her. The petitioner has placed on record photographs and chats between the parties even after the alleged incident which prima facie show that the parties were known to each other and had good relations”. 11. Prosecutrix was medically examined firstly on 15.12.2015. Doctor has written on the MLC that she did not find any external injury mark on the person of the prosecutrix at the time of the examination. There is no medical evidence to support the version of the prosecutrix that accused had attempted to rape her. Accused was also medically examined by doctor on 2.10.2016 at DDU Hospital, New Delhi which State v. Himanshu Kargeti Page 4 of 6 (FIR No.1586/15 PS Uttam Nagar) was a sheer formality.  No obscene photographs/video were recovered during investigation. 12. It is the settled law that order framing the charges does substantially affect the persons and the Court must not automatically frame the charge merely because the prosecution authorities, by relying on the documents referred to in Section 173 Cr.PC, consider it proper to institute the case.  13. Though not referred to or relied upon,  it has been observed by Madhya Pradesh High Court in judgment – Sunder Singh v. State of M.P., Cr.R No.607/2013 decided on 3.9.2013 as under :   “42. The prosecution, having regard to the right of an accused to have a fair investigation, fair inquiry and fair trial as adumbrated under Article 21 of the Constitution of India, cannot at any stage be deprived of taking advantage of the materials which the prosecution itself have placed on record. If upon perusal of the entire materials on record, the court arrives at an opinion that two views are possible, charges can be framed, but if only one and one view is possible to be taken favouring the accused, the court shall not put the accused to harassment by asking him to face a trial. Please see: State of Maharashtra v. Som Nath (1996) 4 SCC 659. In the case at hand, if the Court allowed to asking applicant face the trial on above discussed evidence, definitely it will amount to put the applicant for harassment.”  14. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, after sifting and weighing the evidence for the limited purpose of finding out whether or not a prima facie case is made out against the accused, I am of State v. Himanshu Kargeti Page 5 of 6 (FIR No.1586/15 PS Uttam Nagar) the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against the  accused for framing a charge against him for committing   offences   punishable   under   Sections   376/511   IPC. Accordingly, accused in the present case is discharged for the offence punishable u/s. 376/511 IPC only. All other offences are triable by the Court of Ld.MM. Accused is directed to appear before the Court of concerned Ld.MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi today at 2 pm, who shall proceed further in the matter in accordance with law. Announced today in                      (PRAVEEN KUMAR) open court on 22.3.2017.                     Addl. Sessions Judge (SFTC)   Dwarka Courts, New Delhi.  State v. Himanshu Kargeti Page 6 of 6 (FIR No.1586/15 PS Uttam Nagar)



 four­five days prior to lodging of the complaint to the police when he returned from Haridwar. It is alleged that accused is threatening the prosecutrix of dire consequences and also demanding Rs.85,000/­ from her. On 23.05.2015, prosecutrix got the present FIR registered against the accused on her complaint. 2.  During investigation prosecutrix was medically examined at RTRM Hospital, New Delhi on 24.05.2015. Her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC was recorded by Ld. MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi on 25.05.2015. The statements of witnesses conversant with the facts were recorded. After completion of investigation, charge­sheet was filed against the accused   for   commission   of   offences   punishable   under   Sections 328/376/506 IPC.  3. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. Arvind Vashishth, Ld. Counsel for the accused. 4. Ld. Counsel for the accused has contended that accused has been falsely implicated in this case by the prosecutrix to extort money. According to him, no prima facie case for the alleged offences is made out against the accused and he is liable to be discharged.  5. On the other hand, Ld. APP for the State has contended that there is sufficient material on record for framing charge against the State v. Nishikant Kaushik Page 2  of 8 (FIR No.421/15 PS Najafgarh) accused.  6. I have gone through the case file. The prosecutrix is a married woman. She has not stated the date and month when the accused committed rape upon her. From the Facebook chat record spanning for a period of several dates, it is clear that the relation between the prosecutrix and the accused were consensual and she had also taken a loan from the accused. Few of these chats are reproduced herein below : “10.4.2015 Micky Kaushik ­  Btao na Prosecutrix­ Kya Micky Kaushik – Hsband k sth        Mere toh bura haal h                            Prosecutrix– q Micky Kaushik – Phle aap btao Prosecutrix ­ kuch nhi Micky Kaushik –  plz      Licking      Sucking Prosecutrix – kuch b nhi hua Micky Kaushik – Ki nhi 3 din pehle jb aap bol rhe the thik thak Micky Kaushik – ha no sucking no licking Micky Kaushik – Mn nhi kr rha kya Prosecutrix – na Micky Kaushik – nraj ho Prosecutrix – na nini aayi h Micky Kaushik – Bt kb kroge mn kr rha h shona plz Prosecutrix­ na baby bhot jor se neend aayi h Micky Kaushik – kb kroge” … State v. Nishikant Kaushik Page 3  of 8 (FIR No.421/15 PS Najafgarh)   12.4.2015 Prosecutrix – ab call ya msg mt karna         Micky Kaushik – kb kroge f b pr bt ro rha hu  Prosecutrix – aapko meri kasam rona band kro  Micky Kaushik – Aap bolo kb kroge but no do u luve me … 17.5.2015 Micky Kaushik – Hlo    Plz msg me as soon as possible   Tu kyu khel rhi h sbki life se … 17.5.2015 Prosecutrix – Me mar jaungi ya bunty maar dalega mujhe      Micky Kaushik – Bolo kya kaam kru Prosecutrix – Sbse pehle to na hanuman mandir ja kr hanuman chalisa kro mann se fir dekhna sb thik ho jayega … 17.5.2015 Micky Kaushik – Kya bunty k liye            Vo kbhi nhi sudhr skta Prosecutrix – Bunty ghr me nhi rehte   Raat ko b late aate h   Pta h   Bt agr meri baat pta chali na to mere ghr k b    or buty be mujhe jaan  se mara dega   Me kya kru … 17.5.2015 Micky Kaushik – n ki tk I need my money also          … 17.5.2015 Prosecutrix – Me aapke samne hath jodti hi plzz           Micky Kaushik – Maine sb kuch bta diya kl tk paise n sare seen clear Prosecutrix – Mere pass ya mere ghrwalo k pass ek rs b nhi h  tbhi dono baccho ka  add b nhi krwaya State v. Nishikant Kaushik Page 4  of 8 (FIR No.421/15 PS Najafgarh) Me sb smjhti hu Mujhe sb pta h aap bhot badi problem me ho bt mera ghr ujad jayega me mar gyi to mere  bacche ro ro kr mar jayenge Micky Kaushik – Meri kezu ka same seen h … 19.5.2015 Micky Kaushik – Maine bnty ka notice receive kra h koi h chori ka    Micky Kaushik  ­ Tune kya smjha h mere ko ye bta Micky Kaushik – Chahe kuch bhi kr aate hi mere ko mere      paise de diyo .     Tu kbhi nhi sudhr skti. ... 20.5.15 Micky Kaushik – Mere ko sch me paiso ki bhut jrurt h plz bolo      kb tk aa jaoge  Micky Kaushik – Plz hath jod rha hu khoge roh pare bhi pkd               lunga mere ka mera paise de do n iss prob. Se     niki do. 7. No   gold   chain   or   Rs.10,000/­   were   recovered   during   the investigation which were allegedly taken away by the accused from the prosecutrix. The phone of the accused was not seized. There is nothing on record   that   the   accused   had   clicked   obscene   photographs   of   the prosecutrix. There is no investigation as regards the call detail records of the prosecutrix and the accused. No clothes of the prosecutrix were seized. The FSL result is in negative. There is no medical evidence to support the version of the prosecutrix that she was raped by the accused. State v. Nishikant Kaushik Page 5  of 8 (FIR No.421/15 PS Najafgarh) As per MLC dated 24.5.2015 of the prosecutrix, she was using IUCD for contraception. No fresh external genital injuries were found when the prosecutrix was taken for her medical examination. There is considerable delay in lodging the FIR which has not been adequately explained. She did not raise alarm/hue and cry or lodged report with the police immediately after the alleged incident. 8. The essential ingredient of Section 328 IPC is that the victim should   be   administered   poison   or   any   stupefying   intoxicating   or unwholesome drug or other thing. The forensic examination of the stomach wash in order to determine that the substance that administered was poison is, therefore, imperative for ascertaining the commission of the offence punishable u/s 328 IPC. Admittedly, no stomach wash of the prosecutrix was taken for forensic examination in the present case. The averment made by the prosecutrix that she became unconscious after consuming cold drink cannot be said to be final to reach to the conclusion that the cold drink  administered was either poison or any stupefying intoxicating or unwholesome drug. For taking this view I am supported with the judgment ­  Sanjay Singh v. State, Crl. Appeal No.636/2005 decided on 23.4.2008 by the High Court of Delhi speaking through Hon'ble Mr. Justice S. Murlidhar. As there is no medical evidence on State v. Nishikant Kaushik Page 6  of 8 (FIR No.421/15 PS Najafgarh) record that the substance administered was either poison or stupefying intoxicating or unwholesome drug, no prima facie case u/s 328 IPC can be said to be made out against the accused. 9. Though not referred to or relied upon, it has been observed by the Apex Court in judgment – Prafull Kumar Samal v. Union of India (1979) 3 SCC 4 that the Court has power to sift and weigh the evidence – although for the limited purpose of finding out whether a prima facie case against the accused has been made out or not. It has also been held that where materials placed before the Court disclosed grave suspicion against the accused which has not been properly explained, the Court would be fully justified in framing a charge and proceeding with the trial. By and large, however, if two views are equally possible and the judge is satisfied that the evidence produced before him gives rise to some suspicion, but not grave suspicion against the accused, he will be fully within his right to  discharge the accused.  10. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, after sifting and weighing the evidence for the limited purpose of finding out whether or not a prima facie case is made out against the accused, I am of the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against the  accused for framing a charge against him for State v. Nishikant Kaushik Page 7  of 8 (FIR No.421/15 PS Najafgarh) committing   offences   punishable   under   Sections   328/376/506   IPC. Accordingly, accused in the present case is discharged for the offences punishable u/ss. 328/376/506 IPC. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged.  In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., accused  is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to challenge the present order by filing the appropriate petition in the High Court. Ahlmad is directed to page and bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record. File be consigned to Record Room. Dictated & announced today in                        (PRAVEEN KUMAR) open court on 10.03.2017.                            Addl. Sessions Judge (SFTC)  Dwarka Courts, New Delhi.  State v. Nishikant Kaushik Page 8  of 8 (FIR No.421/15 PS Najafgarh)

 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta J U D G M E N T 1. Accused is facing trial on allegations of committing forcible   sexual   intercourse   and   unnatural   intercourse   with prosecutrix. 2. FIR   was   registered   on   a   written   complaint   of prosecutrix alleging that when she was 8-9 years old, accused was their neighbor. Accused used to commit forcible oral sex and sexual intercourse with her in the absence of her family members. In 2001 accused got married but even after his marriage accused continued to establish physical relations with prosecutrix.  Family of prosecutrix then shifted but there also accused used to come and establish physical relations with her.   Prosecutrix alleged that accused used to tell her that he loves prosecutrix and on false pretext of marrying her used to establish physical relations. On 27.05.2016 accused agreed to marry her but later on he resiled and as such she is making complaint against accused. Judgment 2 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 3. After   registration   of   FIR,   prosecutrix   was   got medically examined.  Her statement was recorded u/s 164 Cr.P.C. Accused was arrested and was charge-sheeted to face trial. Charge for the offence punishable u/s 376/377 IPC was framed against accused to which he pleaded not guilty and claimed trial. 4.   Prosecution examined 13 witnesses.
