On conclusion of prosecution evidence, statement of accused was recorded u/s 313 Cr.P.C.  Accused stated that being neighbor of prosecutrix he was having friendship with her and was helping her financially but after he got married, prosecutrix started intervening in their family and her demands started increasing. When he refused to give financial help, prosecutrix got agitated and she made a false complaint against accused. 6. It is submitted on behalf of accused that though prosecutrix alleged that she was continuously sexually assaulted by accused when she was 8-9 years old but she did not lodge any complaint against accused nor informed her parents about her sexual assault till filing of the complaint and her this conduct Judgment 5 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta shows falsity of her claim regarding her sexual assault.  It has been further contended that prosecutrix herself on 28.05.2016 stated that her dispute with accused stands settled and she did not want any action. It shows that prosecutrix was never sexually assaulted nor harassed by accused. Rather sole intention of prosecutrix was to keep extorting money from accused.  It is further submitted that testimony of prosecutrix in respect of her sexual assault is neither reliable nor trustworthy and hence accused is entitled to be acquitted. 7. Per contra Ld. Addl. PP argued that prosecutrix in all her   statements   maintained   that   accused   established   forcible physical relations with her and even committed unnatural sex with her. Prosecutrix withstood her cross-examination and maintained that she was sexually assaulted by the accused.  It is argued that in light of testimony of prosecutrix and other material witnesses the case of prosecution stands proved against the accused. Judgment 6 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 8. I have heard rival submissions and have gone through the record. 9. Versions   of   prosecutrix:   Prior   to   deposition   of prosecutrix her statement Ex PW1/B was recorded u/s 164 Cr.P.C . It's loose English translation reads as under: “Sunil Gupta is torturing me from my childhood. He is sexually exploiting me. I was 8-9 years old. Since then he used to rub my chest and private part in bad manner. He used to commit sex with me. I was small, I used to get frightened. This way he continued to commit sex with me after frightening & threatening me for many years. He used to commit anal and oral sex with me. He forcibly made me to touch his private parts with my hands. When I became 18 years old, I threatened him to stop following me otherwise, I will tell everybody about your deeds. Then Sunil told me “I love you and I will marry you”. Many times, I told him to stop following me but he continued to torture me. After consuming liquor, he used to reach at ITO Bridge and then used to tell me on phone that “I will commit suicide and say that you are only mine. I will marry you”. He used to say, I am having your photos which I will show to everyone. He got married and have two kids but even then, he did not leave me. Even when his daughter was in Hospital at Paharganj, Judgment 7 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta there also he committed sex with me. On the day of his marriage and first night, he committed forcible sex with me. He used to tell me that I am not happy with my wife Jyoti and after divorcing her I will marry you and used to say to go to Tis Hazari and find out the Divorce procedure. In 2015, I told him enough is enough either to marry me or leave me. Then also he kept averting. In 2016, I told him that I am going far from your life and do not call me. On the same night,   he   called   me   many   times   and   after drinking   liquor   was   threatening   to   commit suicide by coming in front of a truck. In May, I went to his house with my mother to confront him. There his wife called her Jeth-Jethani. They abused me a lot and pushed my mother. I stated that in my childhood he has committed wrong with me. Upon this as well, he and his wife stated that what happened if he has done this. This man has no guilt of what he has done to me. His wife has called me and abused me. Now, he daily threatens me to commit suicide and not to lodge an FIR. Do you want to say anything else? In 2014 regularly he used to reach at bus stand in the morning in front of my house. For four months he stalked me. He followed me till Mujaffarnagar where I went to appear in my examinations. 10. Prosecutrix in her examination-in-chief reiterated the allegations made by her against accused and categorically deposed Judgment 8 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta that in the absence of her parents accused used to come to her room and used to forcibly establish sexual relations with her and also used to insert his private part into her vagina.  Prosecutrix deposed that she was too young and scared by the threat extended by accused as such she used to keep quiet.  Prosecutrix narrated that accused used to take her to secluded places and there also used to commit sexual acts with her. Prosecutrix described that whenever she used to go to the house of accused to bring cold water from his fridge, accused used to follow her and used to establish physical relations with her. 11. Prosecutrix detailed that accused got married on 01.12.2001 and even on the first night of his marriage accused took her to the roof of his house and committed forcible vaginal intercourse with her despite presence of many guests and relatives of accused in the house. Prosecutrix deposed that this continued till she attained the age of 18 years and despite her request accused did not listen.  Ultimately in 2009 she shifted with her family Judgment 9 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta members to a new house. On 06.06.2009 on night of marriage of her brother, accused followed her to her house and had sexual intercourse   with   her.   Thereafter   accused   visited   her   house regularly.   In the year 2006 when daughter of accused was admitted in Pant Hospital, Delhi at that time also accused established forcible sexual relations with her in night and left hospital at 4 a.m. 12. Prosecutrix testified that on 21.10.2012 she went to house of accused and told his wife but before her accused refused to marry prosecutrix.  In the year 2013-14 accused used to take her to hotel where he had taken a room on rent and in the said room accused used to commit oral and vaginal sexual intercourse with her and this continued from the year 2013-16.  In 2015 accused told her that he is not happy with his wife and will divorce her and will then marry prosecutrix.  When wife of accused came to know that accused was meeting her and was having forcible sexual relations with her then wife of accused told prosecutrix that she Judgment 10 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta would commit suicide and kill her children upon which accused told her that he will marry on 27.05.2016.  On 27.05.2016 she mustered courage and informed her mother about the sexual acts upon her by accused and the matter was discussed with her family then she made a call at number 100.  Her medical examination was conducted on 28.05.2016 and accused was called in the police station where accused assured to marry prosecutrix.   Wife of accused and other family members also agreed for their marriage but accused was not willing to divorce his wife and as such prosecutrix lodged complaint on 11.01.2016 as Ex. PW1/A. 13.   After her  examination-in-chief  prosecutrix  was cross-examined at length by Ld Defence counsel and the relevant para's of the cross-examination of the prosecutrix reads as under : “1. I am Law Graduate. I pursued my Law degree from 2009 till 2015 from CCS University, Meerut. It was a five year Law degree course. I cleared my class-XIIth examination in year 2008 from UP Board. Till today, I am not enrolled as an Advocate. Judgment 11 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 3. At Vikaspuri, I was residing in a two room house. I have two elder brothers who are about five years and two years elder to me respectively. Both of them have studied upto 12th standard. I was studying in a different school than to my brothers. I completed my education in four different schools which all were in Vikaspuri. After 9th standard, I did not study in Delhi and I cleared my 10th and 12th examination from UP Board. 6. I know Kamal Kant Narang who is friend of accused.  I may have called him. Vol.: I called him when I used to be in depression and accused avoided my calls. I do not remember his mobile number. 8. It is correct that I did not handover my mobile phone to IO. It is correct that some property talks took place between me, my mother and accused, his family and Kamal Kant on the other side. Accused and his family offered me to pay upto Rs.10 Lakhs for not lodging the FIR.  It is incorrect to suggest that accused never offered me any amount rather I demanded money to withdraw my complaint. 14. I   did   not   mention   in   my   statements Ex.PW1/A and Ex.PW1/B that my grandmother used to remain in the first room of our house and in the second room, I along with my brothers used to stay and the third room was occupied by my parents. When I was aged about 8 – 9 years and was studying in class-II or class-III, my brothers Judgment 12 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta were also studying in the school and my brothers used to go to play in the park in front of our house. I did not state in Ex.PW1/A & B that my grandmother was suffering from polio and was unable to move. 30. I went to Haridwar with Sunil in year 2015 for a single day. In the night, we stayed in a hotel in Haridwar. I told my parents that I was going to appear in my exams and on that pretext, I accompanied accused. It is correct that we also clicked some photographs in a public place together. 32. I might have visited the work place of accused Azadpur 5 or 6 times of my own. Vol.: accused took me with him there number of times which   I   even   cannot   count.   I   continued   to accompany him to his work place even after his marriage till 2015.  35. I   did   not   mention   in   my   subsequent complaint   Ex.PW1/A   or   in   my   statement Ex.PW1/B that accused offered me money or property and for this reason I withdrew the earlier complaint. Vol.: the earlier complaint was withdrawn as accused promised to marry me. Vol.: Despite my legal background, I acted upon the promise extended by accused and his family that accused would marry me being fully aware that accused was a married man… 39. I did not see any document in respect of claimed divorce of accused. I was known to the wife of accused but I never asked her as to whether she was agreed to take divorce from Judgment 13 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta accused. As of today, accused has a son who is about 10 years old. His son calls me 'Bua'. I never told son of accused that I wanted to marry accused. I never told him that his father would get divorce from his mother. Vol.: Of late, I was not meeting the child as we had shifted our residence. Since 2012, we have not been visiting each other's house for family function. At the time of marriage of accused, I danced and enjoyed function. Vol. : At that time, I was merely 13 or 14 years old.  We were having cordial relations and visiting terms with the family of accused till 2013.” 14. Allegations   against   accused   are   appearing   in statements and testimony of prosecutrix goes back to period when prosecutrix was 8-9 years old girl. As per prosecution date of birth of prosecutrix is 01.06.1986 and this means that prosecutrix is alleging that accused sexually assaulted her since year 1995 and complaint in respect of those allegations are made on 11.07.2016 i.e. about 21 years of the alleged incidents of sexual assault. 15. Prosecutrix in her testimony deposed that accused used to come to their house in the absence of her brothers who were studying at that time and then used to forcibly commit oral Judgment 14 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta and vaginal intercourse with her and when she used to resist, accused used to threaten to kill her. Prosecutrix testified that since she was too young and scared by the threat extended by accused, she used to remain quiet. 16. In her examination-in-chief prosecutrix deposed that she was staying in a three rooms flat with her parents, her grandmother, three brothers. She testified that her grandmother was suffering from polio and was unable to move. Her brothers used to go to park in front of their house and she used to remain in home with her grandmother. Prosecutrix alleged that accused used to come and used to forcibly sexual assault her by inserting his private part in her mouth, anus and vagina. 17. During course of her cross-examination, prosecutrix deposed that she was residing in a two room flat. However, PW6 (mother of prosecutrix) deposed that they were residing in a single room Janta Flat and her mother-in-law who was unable to walk Judgment 15 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta always used to remain in house and was not suffering from any mental ailment. If that was the scenario then accused if visited house of prosecutrix, would have no opportunity to find the prosecutrix alone. Prosecutrix was always in company of her grandmother in a single room house. 18. Presuming that prosecutrix being a child was unable to make a complaint against accused about his alleged acts but the fact of the case shows that accused continued to establish physical relations with her till year 2016. Prosecutrix admits that after she attained majority (in year 2004) accused continued to torture her and used to establish oral, anal and vaginal sexual intercourse with her. Prosecutrix admits that she accompanied accused to Haridwar in 2015 and also had established physical relations with accused on number of occasions in room of his hotel from 2011 till 2013 and at that time, she was aware that accused was already a married person.   Judgment 16 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 19. Prosecutrix at no point of time resisted herself to accompany accused to his hotel in Azadpur, rather on one occasion she went to Haridwar with accused by telling his family members that she has to appear in an exam. She also clicked photographs with accused. Conduct of prosecutrix in accompanying accused willfully to his hotel and also at Haridwar shows that she was not offended by any act of accused.  20. Prosecutrix during her cross-examination admitted that in last phase of year 2015 she sent her account number to the mobile phone of the accused through SMS. Accused deposited between Rs.3,000/- to Rs.5,000/- in her account. Though she avoided to give answer as to why accused deposited the said amount in her account but the fact remains that she received money from accused.  Judgment 17 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 21. It is not the case that prosecutrix is an uneducated girl rather it is matter of record that she has completed her LL.B in year 2015. Prosecutrix was fully aware about the marriage of accused rather one of her allegation is that accused established sexual relations with her on the night of his wedding. Therefore, it has to be concluded that prosecutrix was fully aware of the consequences of accompanying accused (a married person) and having physical relations with him.  22. Prosecutrix is a fully grown up lady, continued her intimate   relationship  with   accused   which   shows   that   her relationship was not an act induced by misconception of any fact. If the story set up by the prosecutrix herself in the court is to be believed, it does come to the fore that the two were in a relationship. Having accompanying accused to Haridwar and to his Hotel  at Azadpur she knew the likely outcome of her action. She knew what are consequences of spending night with a male.  Judgment 18 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 23. Entire circumstances discussed above and which have come to the fore from the testimony of none else but the prosecutrix, it cannot be said that the sexual intercourse was without her consent. The act seems to be consensual in nature. 24. Promise to marry: Prosecutrix alleged that accused allured her in this relationship and promised to marry her. In this regard, prosecutrix in her cross- examination deposed as under: 35. ……. the earlier complaint was withdrawn as accused promised to marry me. Vol.: Despite my legal background, I acted upon the promise extended by accused and his family that accused would marry me being fully aware that accused was a married man… 39.     I did not see any document in respect of claimed divorce of accused. I was known to the wife of accused but I never asked her as to whether she was agreed to take divorce from accused. 25. Prosecutrix pursued her law course. She was in visiting terms with accused. Prosecutrix was acquainted with wife of accused. She had every opportunity to find out from wife of Judgment 19 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta accused whether there was any likelihood of divorce between them or not but prosecutrix made no effort to clarify the position from wife of accused. Thus, it is not the case where consent was given by prosecutrix believing the accused's promise to marry her.  26. In  Gaurav Maggo v. State, Crl. A. No.369/2014, decided by Hon'ble High Court of Delhi on 29.05.2015, it has been held as under : “There is nothing in her evidence to demonstrate that she was incapable of understanding the nature and implications of the act which she consented to. Her consent for physical relations (if any) was an act of conscious reason. If a fully grown up lady consents to the act of sexual intercourse on a promise to marry and continues to indulge in such activity for long, it is an act of promiscuity on her part and not an act induced by misconception of fact.” 27. In present case prosecutrix being well aware of marital status of accused, having mature understanding cannot be in any kind of misconception while entering into relationship with accused. At no point of time, question of her marriage with accused was deliberated upon by family of accused. Thus, it also Judgment 20 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta cannot be said that the consent for sexual intercourse had been given by the prosecutrix under misconception of marriage. 28. Lodging of FIR: Prosecutrix in her initial complaint Ex PW1/A made on 11.07.2016 gave reason for making complaint against accused by stating that on 27.05.2016, she made a complaint against accused and also got medically examined but at that time accused & his wife agreed for her marriage with accused but later on accused is refusing to marry her.  29. Prosecutrix   deposed   that   accused   was   sexually assaulted her since she was 8-9 years old girl. Going by the age of prosecutrix, allegation against accused is that he was assaulting her since year 1995 but complaint in respect of those allegations are made on 11.07.2016 i.e. about 21 years of the alleged incidents of sexual assault. It is evident from testimony of prosecutrix that she continued relations with accused despite her sexual assault by accused.  Judgment 21 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 30. On   MLC   (Ex   PW1/D1)   of   prosecutrix   dated 28.05.2016, she made an endorsement at point 'X' that matter between them and accused got settled and she does not want any action against accused. As per prosecutrix at that time accused and his wife agreed to marry accused with her. 31. But   the   reason   for   withdrawing   her   previous complaint against accused is hardly believable in light of the fact that accused was a married man and even if he had agreed to marry prosecutrix then also his marriage to prosecutrix was not legally permissible. Prosecutrix being herself a Law Graduate was aware of the legal position and could not have acted upon this kind of arrangement. 32. Prosecution has relied upon the case titled as Som Dev Vs. State of NCT of Delhi (Criminal appeal no. 291/2012) wherein Hon'ble High Court of Delhi in Para 13 of the said judgment has held as under:- Judgment 22 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta “13. Delay in lodging the FIR is inconsequential. In fact, there is no delay in putting the police machinery into motion. The appellant and 'X' were on friendly terms and physical relations on 21.05.2009 were consensual.  From the very inception, X's case was that she had consented for physical relations on the promise to marry.  There was, thus no occasion/reason to lodge complaint soon after establishing physical relations. 'X' had no reasons to suspect that the promise held out by the appellant would not be fulfilled.  She was expected to wait for his response for reasonable period. Call details record (Ex. PW-7/D) reveals that on 22.05.2009 both were in touch and the appellant had made four telephone calls to her during night time; on 23.05.2009, he made two calls at 10.50 & 11.01 hours; on 25.05.2009, six calls were made to 'X' at different times of the day; the last call being at 22:37 hours. Thereafter, frequency   to contact 'X' decreased  and  on  26.05.2009  &  02.06.2009  and 06.06.2009, only one call each was made. When the appellant started ignoring her calls and did not contact her 'X' immediately lodged complaint (Ex. PW- 1/A) on 09.06.2009.   Even in that complaint, she desired the Investigating Officer to ask the appellant to marry her. Apparently 'X' who wanted to marry the appellant was in no haste to lodge complaint against him.  She is a victim of circumstances. Despite her lodging complaint (Ex. PW-1/A) on 09.06.2009, the Investigating Agency did not register FIR and kept it 'pending'.   Only   when   vigilance   enquiry   found substance in the complaint, the FIR was lodged on 23.10.2009.”   Judgment 23 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 33. I am afraid that the aforesaid judgment cited on behalf of prosecution does not help its cause for the simple reason that in the present case the explanation given by prosecutrix that she did not lodge any complaint for 21 years and her version that she was under impression that accused would marry her is found improbable and not worthy of any credit. Facts of the case demonstrates that there is substantial unexplained delay in lodging of FIR. 34. From above stated discussions it emerges that : i)   Prosecutrix   is   law   graduate   having   mature understanding.  ii) She was aware about marital status of accused. iii)   Though   prosecutrix   claims   that   accused   sexually exploited her in her childhood but prosecutrix continued her relationship with accused. iv)   Version   of   prosecutrix   that   she   continued   her relationship on promise to marry is found not believable. v) Prosecutrix accepted financial assistance from accused, went to his place of work and spent a night with accused being   fully   aware   of   his   marital   status   shows   her inclination towards accused. vi) There is un-explanied delay in lodging of FIR. Judgment 24 of  25 SC No: 93/17 State Vs. Sunil Kumar Gupta 35. Conclusion:   From   aforesaid   discussions,   it   is evident that prosecution has failed to prove charges against accused. Accordingly, accused stands acquitted. His surety is discharged. Bail bond stands canceled. Accused is  directed to furnish a personal and surety bond in sum of Rs. 10,000/-  under provisions of Section 437-A Cr.P.C  which shall remain in force for period of six months.      File be consigned to record room. Announced in the open court on 3rd day of January, 2018.          GAUTAM MANAN               Addl. Sessions Judge (SFTC)                      South-West, Dwarka Courts, Delhi.                  Judgment 25 of  25

 The statement of the prosecutrix under Section 164 Cr.P.C. was also recorded wherein she disclosed her age as 18 years and stated that she had left her home about six months back as her family members used to give beatings to her and that after leaving home, she had solemnized marriage with the accused and started residing with him. During the course of investigation, Sections 376 IPC and 4  POCSO Act were added. After the completion of investigation, the charge sheet was filed. 2. On 05.04.2017, the charge for the commission of offence punishable under Section 363/376 IPC and Section 6 POCSO Act was framed against the accused to which he pleaded not guilty and claimed trial.                                             3. The prosecution examined the prosecutrix, her mother and brother­in­ law (jija) as PW1 to PW3 respectively. Since the prosecutrix and her mother did not support the case of the prosecution, the remaining prosecution evidence was closed and the statement of the accused under Section 313 Cr.P.C. was dispensed with.          4. I have heard the Addl. PP for the State and the counsel for the accused. The material on record has also been perused.  5. In her testimony, the prosecutrix (PW1) deposed that she used to reside with her brother­in­law (jija) and since he used to give beatings to her, she left the home and went to Bihar where she got married with the accused, who was the friend of her brother­in­law. She further deposed that the accused had not made any physical relation with her prior to Sessions Case No. 85/2017            State Vs. Raj Kumar @ Raju                     Page No. 2/7 the marriage nor he had enticed her to leave the house of her brother­in­ law. She also deposed that her mother had wrongly mentioned her age in the school record and she was, infact, aged around 18 years. She was cross­examined by the Addl. PP wherein she denied that she had left the house at the instance of the accused or that he had taken her to Bihar. She also denied the suggestion that she was not telling her correct age and stated that she was 1 ½ years younger to her elder married sister, who was 20 years old. The mother of the prosecutrix, who was examined as PW2, also admitted in her cross­examination that after returning home, the prosecutrix had revealed her that she had left the house on account of ill treatment given to her by her brother­in­law and had got married with the accused out of her own volition. She further stated that since the accused had not done anything wrong with the prosecutrix, she did want any action against him. She also admitted that though the prosecutrix was born in the year 1999 but she had mentioned the year of her birth as 2004 in the school record in order to procure her admission in Ist class. She also affirmed that her eldest daughter was about 20­22 years old and the prosecutrix was about two years younger to her. Besides the prosecutrix and her mother, the prosecution has examined the complainant i.e. the brother­in­law of the prosecutrix as PW3. He deposed that after lodging the complaint, he came to know that the prosecutrix was residing with the accused in Bihar and that when he went to Bihar to bring her, she refused to come to Delhi by stating that she had solemnized marriage with the accused. Sessions Case No. 85/2017            State Vs. Raj Kumar @ Raju                     Page No. 3/7 6. Addl. PP has argued that even if, the prosecutrix has not supported the case of the prosecution, considering her age as borne out from her first attended school certificate, she was minor at the time of incident in question and her consent was immaterial in the eyes of law and, therefore, the accused is guilty of the offences for which he has been charged.  On the other hand, the defence counsel has disputed the age of the prosecutrix as mentioned in her school record on the ground that the mother of the prosecutrix had not produced any certificate issued by the municipal corporation or any other statutory authority with regard to the date of birth of the prosecutrix. He has submitted that as the prosecutrix and her mother have not supported the case of the prosecution in their testimonies, the accused be acquitted of the charged offence. 7. In order to prove the age of the prosecutrix, the investigating agency has placed on record her first attended school certificate wherein her date of birth has been mentioned as 10.02.2004. The said age of the prosecutrix had been entered in the school record on the basis of an affidavit submitted by the mother of the prosecutrix and not on the basis of any certificate issued by the municipal corporation or any other statutory authority. Needless to say, the age of the prosecutrix is within the special knowledge of her mother. Since in her testimony, the mother of the prosecutrix (PW2) has categorically deposed that the prosecutrix was born in the year 1999 and that she had furnished wrong Sessions Case No. 85/2017            State Vs. Raj Kumar @ Raju                     Page No. 4/7 date of her birth in the school record in order to procure her admission in Ist class, the school certificate produced by the prosecution can not be relied upon as conclusive proof of the age of the prosecutrix. Infact, the said document has to be discarded in view of the deposition of PW2 i.e. the mother of the prosecutrix. As the incident in question took place in the year 2016 and the prosecutrix was born in the year 1999 as deposed by her mother, it is evident that she was about 17 years old at the relevant time.  8.  From the deposition of the prosecutrix, it is clear that she had left the custody of her lawful guardian on her own. The reason for doing so was that she was not happy at her maternal home. After leaving her maternal home, she went to Bihar where she got married with the accused. In S. Varadarajan v. State of Madras, AIR 1965 SC 942, while making   a   distinction   between   'taking'   and   allowing   a   minor   to accompany a person, the Apex Court has held that where the minor leaves her father's protection knowing and having capacity to know the full import of what she is doing and voluntarily joins the accused without any force or inducement, the accused can not be said to have taken her away from the keeping of her lawful guardian. In the present case, the prosecutrix was on the verge of attaining majority at the time of leaving her maternal home. Considering her age and the fact that she used to reside in the Capital city of Delhi, there can be no doubt that she had the capacity to understand the import of her acts. There is nothing on record to suggest that the accused had played any role to Sessions Case No. 85/2017            State Vs. Raj Kumar @ Raju                     Page No. 5/7 influence the decision of the prosecutrix to abandon the custody of her mother.  The accused was under no obligation to take the prosecutrix back to the custody of her lawful guardian. The mere act of the accused in fulfilling the desire of the prosecutrix to marry him after she had left the custody of her guardian falls short of 'taking' or 'enticing' within the meaning of Section 361 IPC and thereby, the offence under Section 363 IPC is not made out against the accused.                    As far as the charge for the offence under Section 6 POCSO Act is concerned, the issue which arises for consideration is whether a man who establishes sexual relations with his wife below 18 years but above 15 years of age can be held guilty for the commission of offence of penetrative sexual assault. The above issue came up for consideration before   the   Delhi   High   Court   in   Criminal   Revision   Petition No. 266/2014 titled as State of NCT of Delhi v. Umesh. In the said case, the accused, who had been charge­sheeted under Section 363/376 IPC and Section 4 POCSO Act, had been discharged by the Sessions Court by relying upon the statement of the child victim recorded under Section 164 Cr.P.C. wherein she had stated that she had voluntarily gone out of the lawful guardianship of her parents as they used to beat her regularly and that thereafter, she had met the accused with whom she got married and the sexual relations between them were established pursuant to the marriage. Though it was argued before the Hon'ble High Court that the consent of the victim, who was minor, can not be termed as valid consent, however, taking note of the fact that the prosecutrix had given her age as 15 years in her statement under Sessions Case No. 85/2017            State Vs. Raj Kumar @ Raju                     Page No. 6/7 Section 164 Cr.P.C. coupled with the fact that she had established physical relations with the accused on her own after the marriage, the revision petition was dismissed by the Court vide judgment dated 21.07.2015. The factual matrix of the case on hand is almost similar. The prosecutrix (PW1) has categorically stated that she had married the accused of her free will and no sexual relations were made by the accused with her before the marriage. Considering the same, it can not be said that the accused was on the wrong side of law.    9.  In the light of the above discussion, the accused Raj Kumar @ Raju is acquitted of the charge for the commission of offences punishable under Sections 363/376 IPC and Section 6 POCSO Act. Personal bond in terms of Section 437A Cr.P.C. furnished on behalf of the accused has been accepted, which shall remain in force for a period of six months from today. Pronounced in the open court.                       (SANJAY GARG) Dated:  26.10.2017                            Additional Sessions Judge­01,                Dwarka Courts, New Delhi.   Sessions Case No. 85/2017            State Vs. Raj Kumar @ Raju                     Page No. 7/7

 3. During investigation prosecutrix was medically examined at DDU Hospital, Hari Nagar, New Delhi on 28.05.2016. Her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC was recorded by Ld. MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi on 30.05.2016. The statements of witnesses conversant with the facts were recorded. After completion of investigation, a charge­sheet was filed against the accused for commission of offences under Section 376 IPC.  4. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State; Sh. Rishipal Singh, Ld. Counsel for the prosecutrix and Sh. Ravinder Yadav, Ld. Counsel for the accused. 5. Ld. Counsel for the accused has contended that accused has been falsely implicated in this case. According to him, if a grown up girl has consented to sexual intercourse with a person who held out false promise to marry her, it would not amount to consenting under any misconception of fact u/s 90 IPC and, as such, no offence of rape can be said to have been committed. According to him, no prima facie case for the alleged offence is made out against the accused and he is liable to be discharged.  6. On the other hand, Ld. APP for the State and Ld. Counsel for the prosecutrix have contended that there is sufficient material on record for framing charges against the accused. State v. Sudhir Maan.                                                                                                         Page 2 of 8 (FIR No.390/16, PS Bindapur) 7. I have gone through the case file. The FIR in criminal case is an extremely vital and valuable piece of evidence for the purpose of corroborating the oral evidence adduced at the trial. It is well settled proposition of law that a mere delay itself cannot be a ground to disbelieve the entire case of the prosecution. The effect of delay is to be understood in the light of the plausibility of the explanation forthcoming and must depend for consideration on all the facts and circumstances of a given case. Though not referred to or relied upon, in case of Dilawar v. State of Delhi, 2007 Cri.LJ 4709,  it has been held by the Apex Court that in criminal trial one of the cardinal principles for the Court is to look for plausible   explanation   for   the   delay   in   lodging   the   report.   Delay sometimes affords opportunity to the complainant to make deliberation upon   the   complaint   and   to   make   embellishment   or   even   make fabrications. 8. The delay of one or two days in lodging the FIR may be bonafide, reasonable and justified in the facts and circumstances of a given case. However, in the present case there is inordinate delay in lodging the FIR.  9. In her complaint on which present FIR was lodged it is alleged that accused raped her on the pretext of marriage. The prosecutrix State v. Sudhir Maan.                                                                                                         Page 3 of 8 (FIR No.390/16, PS Bindapur) is aged about 30 years and is a married lady having two kids. Thus, the version of the prosecutrix that accused had physical relations with her on the pretext of marriage is not believable. The relationship continued for sufficient duration and at no stage she raised alarm/hue and cry or lodged report with the police against alleged rape. The accused and the prosecutrix, after lodging of the present FIR, approached the High Court of Delhi for quashing of the FIR. However, the said petition was dismissed as withdrawn. At the time of hearing of the bail application, the Ld. A.S.J. observed as under : “The IO present in person today and she identifies  the prosecutrix and on inquiry from the prosecutrix she submits that matter has been settled with the applicant as FIR was got lodged due to some misunderstanding and they will again approach the Hon'ble High Court of Delhi after the charge­sheet is filed in this case.” 10. The prosecutrix was mature enough to fully understand as to what was happening between the two. Where was the compulsion for her to establish physical relations first without ensuring that the accused was willing to perform marriage with her?  In the facts and circumstances of this case, it was an act of promiscuity on the part of the prosecutrix and not an act induced by misconception of fact. Though not referred to or relied upon, in similar circumstances, in judgment – Gaurav Maggo v. State v. Sudhir Maan.                                                                                                         Page 4 of 8 (FIR No.390/16, PS Bindapur) State,   Crl.   A.   No.369/2014,   decided   by   High   Court   of   Delhi   on 29.05.2015, it has been held as under : “There is nothing in her evidence to demonstrate that she was incapable of understanding the nature and implications of the act which she consented to. Her consent for physical relations (if any) was an act of conscious reason. If a fully grown up lady consents to the act of sexual intercourse on a promise to marry and continues to indulge in such activity for long, it is an act of promiscuity on her part and not an act induced by misconception of fact.”  11. Prosecutrix was medically examined firstly on 28.05.2016. Doctor has written on the MLC that she did not find any external injury mark on the person of the prosecutrix at the time of the examination. There is no medical evidence to support the version of the prosecutrix that she was raped as she was taken to the hospital after considerable delay. Accused was also medically examined by doctor on 30.09.2016 at DDU Hospital, New Delhi which was a sheer formality. 12. It is the settled law that order framing the charges does substantially affect the persons and the Court must not automatically frame the charge merely because the prosecution authorities, by relying on the documents referred to in Section 173 Cr.PC, consider it proper to institute the case.  13. Though not referred to or relied upon,  it has been observed by Madhya Pradesh High Court in judgment – Sunder Singh v. State of State v. Sudhir Maan.                                                                                                         Page 5 of 8 (FIR No.390/16, PS Bindapur) M.P., Cr.R No.607/2013 decided on 3.9.2013 as under :   “42. The prosecution, having regard to the right of an accused to have a fair investigation, fair inquiry and fair trial as adumbrated under Article 21 of the Constitution of India, cannot at any stage be deprived of taking advantage of the materials which the prosecution itself have placed on record. If upon perusal of the entire materials on record, the court arrives at an opinion that two views are possible, charges can be framed, but if only one and one view is possible to be taken favouring the accused, the court shall not put the accused to harassment by asking him to face a trial. Please see: State of Maharashtra v. Som Nath (1996) 4 SCC 659. In the case at hand, if the Court allowed to asking applicant face the trial on above discussed evidence, definitely it will amount to put the applicant for harassment.”  14. Though not referred to or relied upon, in judgment­ Jayanti Rani Panda v. State of W.B., 1984 Crl. Law Journal 1535 it has been held that if a grown up girl has consented to sexual intercourse with a person who held out false promise to marry her it would not amount to consenting under any misconception of fact under Section 90 IPC and sexual intercourse by the man under these circumstance would not be an offence of rape as defined in Section 375 IPC. Though not referred to or relied upon, in similar circumstances, in judgment ­ State v. Anupam Bhardwaj, Criminal Revision P. No. 4/2017, decided on 3.1.2017, our High Court of Delhi speaking through Hon'ble Mr. Justice Vipin Sanghi has upheld the order of the trial court discharging the accused in a rape State v. Sudhir Maan.                                                                                                         Page 6 of 8 (FIR No.390/16, PS Bindapur) case. 15. After examining the documentary as well as oral evidence which the prosecution proposes to adduce to prove the guilt of the accused, even if fully accepted, before it is challenged by cross­ examination or rebutted by defence evidence, if any, is not showing that accused   committed   the   alleged   offence   for   which   they   are   being prosecuted. 16.  Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, after sifting and weighing the evidence for the limited purpose of finding out whether or not a prima facie case is made out against the accused, I am of the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against the  accused for framing a charge against him for committing offence punishable under Sections 376 IPC. Accordingly, accused in the present case is discharged for the offence punishable u/s. 376 IPC. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged. In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., accused  is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to challenge the present order by filing the appropriate petition in the High Court. Ahlmad is directed to page and State v. Sudhir Maan.                                                                                                         Page 7 of 8 (FIR No.390/16, PS Bindapur) bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record. File be consigned to Record Room. Announced today in                      (PRAVEEN KUMAR) open court on 27.3.2017.                     Addl. Sessions Judge (SFTC)   Dwarka Courts, New Delhi.  State v. Sudhir Maan.                                                                                                         Page 8 of 8 (FIR No.390/16, PS Bindapur)

 for commission of offence punishable u/s 376/506 IPC. 3. During investigation prosecutrix was medically examined at DDU Hospital, Hari Nagar, New Delhi on 02.08.2016. Her statement u/s 164 Cr.PC was recorded by Ld. MM, Dwarka Courts, New Delhi on 05.08.2016. The statements of witnesses conversant with the facts were recorded. After completion of investigation, charge­sheet was filed against   the   accused   for   commission   of   offences   punishable   under Sections 376/506 IPC.  4. I have heard Ms. Satvinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. Divyesh Pratap Singh, Ld. Counsel for the accused. 5. Ld. Counsel for the accused has contended that accused has been falsely implicated in this case by the prosecutrix. It is contended that in the hotel at Massourie two rooms were booked in the name of the accused and no physical relations were established by the accused with the prosecutrix. It is further contended that although prosecutrix and the accused were in love with each other but their marriage could not take place as they belonged to different castes. As the accused decided to get married to some other girl, the prosecutrix lodged the present false case to put pressure upon him. According to him, no prima facie case for the alleged offences is made out against the accused and he is liable to be State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 2  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur) discharged. In support of his contentions, Ld. Counsel has relied upon judgments – Rohit Chauhan v. State of NCT of Delhi, 2013 (4) JCC 2801; Deepak Gulati v. State of Haryana, (2013) 7 SCC 675; Prashant Bharti v. State of NCT of Delhi, Crl. Appeal No. 175 of 2013, decided by the Apex Court on 23.1.2013; Sujit Ranjan v. State, Crl. Appeal No. 248/2010, decided by High Court of Delhi on 27.01.2011; Uday v. State of Karnataka, (2003) 4 SCC 46 and Sunder Singh v. State of Madhya Pradesh, Crl. Revision No. 607 of 2013, decided by High Court of Madhya Pradesh on 3.9.2013.  6. On the other hand, Ld. APP for the State has contended that there is sufficient material on record for framing charge against the accused. 7. I have gone through the case file. The FIR in criminal case is an extremely vital and valuable piece of evidence for the purpose of corroborating the oral evidence adduced at the trial. It is well settled proposition of law that a mere delay itself cannot be a ground to disbelieve the entire case of the prosecution. The effect of delay is to be understood in the light of the plausibility of the explanation forthcoming and must depend for consideration on all the facts and circumstances of a given case. Though not referred to or relied upon, in case of Dilawar v. State of Delhi, 2007 Cri.LJ 4709,  it has been held by the Apex Court that State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 3  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur) in criminal trial one of the cardinal principles for the Court is to look for plausible   explanation   for   the   delay   in   lodging   the   report.   Delay sometimes affords opportunity to the complainant to make deliberation upon   the   complaint   and   to   make   embellishment   or   even   make fabrications. 8. The delay of one or two days in lodging the FIR may be bonafide, reasonable and justified in the facts and circumstances of a given case. However, in the present case there is inordinate delay in lodging the FIR.  9. In her complaint on which present FIR was lodged, it is alleged that accused raped the prosecutrix on the pretext of marriage. The prosecutrix was mature enough to fully understand as to what was happening between the two. Where was the compulsion for her to establish physical relations first without ensuring that the accused was willing to perform marriage with her ? Though not referred to or relied upon, in similar circumstances,   in   judgment   –  Gaurav   Maggo   v.   State,   Crl.   A. No.369/2014, decided by High Court of Delhi on 29.05.2015, it has been held as under : “There is nothing in her evidence to demonstrate that she was incapable of understanding the nature and implications of the act which she consented to. Her consent for physical relations (if any) was an act of conscious reason. If a fully grown up lady consents to the act of sexual intercourse on a promise to marry and continues to indulge in such activity for long, it is an act of promiscuity on her part and not an State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 4  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur) act induced by misconception of fact.”  10. Prosecutrix was medically examined firstly on 02.08.2016. Doctor has written on the MLC that she did not find any external injury mark on the person of the prosecutrix at the time of the examination. There is no medical evidence to support the version of the prosecutrix that she was raped as she was taken to the hospital after considerable delay. Accused was also medically examined by doctor on 08.09.2016 at DDU Hospital, New Delhi which was a sheer formality. It is the case of the prosecution itself that the prosecutrix was well aware of the fact that the accused was already engaged and was about to get married very soon. Even after being acquainted with this fact, the prosecutrix joined the accused on a trip to Massourie. No complaint was made by the prosecutrix at the time of incident or during her stay at Massourie despite the fact that she stayed there for four consecutive days where the accused allegedly committed rape upon her. The prosecutrix is a working lady and not an illiterate or vulnerable woman that she would not raise her voice on being ravished by the accused for four days. PW Suprabhas Sarkar   in his statement u/s 161 Cr.PC has stated that accused had booked two room numbers 107 and 108 in their hotel from 15.6.2016 to 17.6.2016 where two boys and two girls had stayed. He has categorically stated that none of them lodged State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 5  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur) any complaint with the hotel during their stay. PW Manish is the other person   who   had   accompanied   the   accused   and   the   prosecutrix   to Massourie and had stayed in the same hotel. In his statement u/s 161 Cr.PC dated 18.09.2016, he has stated as under :  “Mai gaadi drive karke gaya tha to mujhe nind aane lagi. Mai tab kareeb 12 baje jakar ek kamre mai so gaya. Mujhe Brij ne kaha ke tu chal mai bhi tere paas aakar sounga. Mujhe neend aa gai thi. Jab maine subah uthkar dekha to Brij mere kamre mai hi so raha tha. Mujhe nahi pata vo rat ko kahan tha. Agle din bhi raat ko ye hi hua tha. Pahle hum sab baate kar rahe the fir mai to jakar so gaya. Mujhe nahi pata Brij kab aaya tha parantu subah mere kamre mai tha. Vo dono Ladkiya ek kamre mai thi. Mai Ponty naam ki ladki ko nahi janta hoo ki vah kaun hai. Maine use Shikayatkarta ke ghar se pick up kiya tha. Vahi drop kiya tha.” 11.  The statement of the other girl namely Ponty, who was known to the prosecutrix, was not recorded during the investigation of the present case. There is no explanation from the side of the prosecution as to why her statement was not recorded. 12. It   is   the   settled   law   that   order   framing   the   charges   does substantially affect the persons and the Court must not automatically frame the charge merely because the prosecution authorities, by relying on the documents referred to in Section 173 Cr.PC, consider it proper to institute the case.  13. It has been observed by Madhya Pradesh High Court in judgment – State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 6  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur) Sunder Singh  (supra) as under :   “42. The prosecution, having regard to the right of an accused to have a fair investigation, fair inquiry and fair trial as adumbrated under Article 21 of the Constitution of India, cannot at any stage be deprived of taking advantage of the materials which the prosecution itself have placed on record. If upon perusal of the entire materials on record, the court arrives at an opinion that two views are possible, charges can be framed, but if only one and one view is possible to be taken favouring the accused, the court shall not put the accused to harassment by asking him to face a trial. Please see: State of Maharashtra v. Som Nath (1996) 4 SCC 659. In the case at hand, if the Court allowed to asking applicant face the trial on above discussed evidence, definitely it will amount to put the applicant for harassment.”  14. Though not referred to or relied upon, in judgment­ Jayanti Rani Panda v. State of W.B., 1984 Crl. Law Journal 1535 it has been held that if a grown up girl has consented to sexual intercourse with a person who held out false promise to marry her it would not amount to consenting under any misconception of fact under Section 90 IPC and sexual intercourse by the man under these circumstance would not be an offence of rape as defined in Section 375 IPC. Though not referred to or relied upon, in similar circumstances, in judgment ­ State v. Anupam Bhardwaj, Criminal Revision P. No. 4/2017, decided on 3.1.2017, our High Court of Delhi speaking through Hon'ble Mr. Justice Vipin Sanghi has upheld the order of the trial court discharging the accused in a rape case. State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 7  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur) 15. For an offence u/s 506 IPC, threat must be with an intention to cause alarm to the person threatened. Mere expression of any words without any intention to cause alarm would not be sufficient to bring in the application of Section 506 IPC. There is nothing on record that any alarm was caused to the prosecutrix. Thus, ingredients of Section 506 IPC are also not attracted. Though not referred to or relied upon, for taking this view I am supported with the judgment­ Amitabh Adhar  Vs. NCT of Delhi 2000 (56) DRJ 220.  16. After examining the documentary as well as oral evidence which the prosecution proposes to adduce to prove the guilt of the accused, even if fully accepted, before it is challenged by cross­examination or rebutted by defence evidence, if any, is not showing that accused committed the alleged offence for which they are being prosecuted. 17.  Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, after sifting and weighing the evidence for the limited purpose of finding out whether or not a prima facie case is made out against the accused, I am of the opinion that the materials placed before the Court do not disclose the grave suspicion against the  accused for framing a charge against him for committing offence punishable under Sections 376 IPC. Accordingly, accused in the present case is discharged for the offence punishable u/s. State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 8  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur) 376 IPC. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged.  In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., accused  is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to challenge the present order by filing the appropriate petition in the High Court. Ahlmad is directed to page and bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record. File be consigned to Record Room. Announced today in                      (PRAVEEN KUMAR) open court on 12.4.2017.                     Addl. Sessions Judge (SFTC)   Dwarka Courts, New Delhi.  State v. Brij  Kishore Mishra  Page 9  of 9 (FIR No.511/16 PS Binda Pur)

 SC No. 70/17 State Vs. Gaurav Gulati     IN THE COURT OF SH. GAUTAM MANAN  ADDITIONAL SESSIONS JUDGE-FAST TRACK SOUTH-WEST, DWARKA, NEW DELHI             In the matter of:- S. C. No. 70/17 FIR No. 510/16 Police Station      Vikas Puri Under Section 376 IPC                          State                  Versus                  Gaurav Gulati @ Arush Malik                      S/o Sh. Sanjeev Gulati                R/o H.No. H-173,   East Shalimar Bagh                   New Delhi.  .....Accused   Date of institution 06.02.2017 Judgment reserved on  15.03.2018 Judgment Pronounced on  04.04.2018 Decision Acquittal Judgment 1 of 20  SC No. 70/17 State Vs. Gaurav Gulati J U D G M E N T 1.  Accused is facing trial on allegations of committing repeated rape on prosecutrix. 2.  FIR in question was registered on complaint of prosecutrix alleging that she met accused Gaurav Gulati but at the time of meeting her in 2011 he disclosed his name as Arush Malik. At the time of her first meeting at Barista, prosecutrix told accused that she does not want to indulge in a fling or time pass relationship. Accused assured her that he is serious about his relationship and proposed her for marriage.  In February 2012 being aware about their relationship and being elder daughter of her parents were insisting to get married to accused or they will look for a match for her.  Accused then told them that he is serious about prosecutrix and wanted to marry her. In November 2013 accused took her to Connaught Place and established sexual relations in his car with her near a restaurant by forcing and assuring to marry her.  Judgment 2 of 20  SC No. 70/17 State Vs. Gaurav Gulati   In January 2014 her friend told her that accused is having Facebook account in name of Gaurav Gulati and then she asked about his real identity after which accused told her that his name is Gaurav Gulati. After which, accused met her father and assured him that he would marry prosecutrix.  Prosecutrix alleged that accused gave his residential and factory address to her father which was found fake. Her father after searching factory of father of accused went there.  Accused and his father assured father of prosecutrix that accused wanted to marry prosecutrix and his father has no objection.  However, they kept on making excuses. On 19.09.2015 prosecutrix met accused and his mother at Barista and on 26.09.2015 accused and his family members went to the home of prosecutrix.   Their meeting was fine. On 06.10.2015 prosecutrix called accused on his birthday but he started accusing prosecutrix and also talked rudely to her parents.  After that her father continuously met parents of accused and ultimately in January 2016 they demanded Rs. 30 lacs from her father and without informing prosecutrix and her parents on 20.04.2016 Judgment 3 of 20  SC No. 70/17 State Vs. Gaurav Gulati accused got married to another girl.   Prosecutrix alleged that accused and his parents cheated her by making false promises of marriage to her and made physical relations with her. 3.  Accused was charge-sheeted for offence punishable u/s 376 IPC.  Charge for offence punishable u/s 376 IPC was framed against accused on 04.03.2017 to which he pleaded not guilty and claimed trial.  4.  Prosecution examined 9 witnesses.
