 (name withheld) at Mathura, U.P and they stayed there together in a single room. In the morning of 04.03.2012, accused married her at Bankey Bihari Mandir, U.P. In April 2012, accused came to meet her and made physical relations with her. On 12.06.2012, they went to Char Dham Yatra and stayed together for ten days where he made physical relations with her. It is the case of the prosecution that accused   also   made   physical   relations   with   the   prosecutrix   on 12.09.2012,   19.11.2012   and   29.12.2012   at   different   places. Prosecutrix was also threatened of dire consequences by the accused if the matter was reported to the police. 3. On the complaint of the prosecutrix, FIR was initially registered for the commission of offences punishable u/ss. 498A/506 IPC. 4. The   matter   was   investigated   by   the   police.   During investigation, statement of the prosecutrix was got recorded u/s.164 Cr.P.C. Accused was arrested. The statements of the witnesses were recorded. The prosecutrix as well as accused were got medically examined.  After   completing   investigation   and   conducting   other necessary   formalities,   chargesheet   was   filed   in   the   court   for commission of offences punishable u/ss  376/420/354/506  IPC. 5. After supplying the copies of the documents to the accused u/s 207 Cr.PC, Ld Metropolitan Magistrate committed the present case to the Court of Sessions. 6. Charge u/s 376 IPC against accused was framed to which he pleaded not guilty and claimed trial. He was accordingly put to State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 2  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. trial. 7. Trial proceeded and in the course of trial, prosecution in order to substantiate its case against the accused, examined fifteen witnesses in all. PW1 is the prosecutrix who has narrated the incident. PW2 Sushil Kumar, PW­3 Veena and PW­8 Sunny Rajpal are the brother, sister and nephew of the prosecutrix. PW­4 Vijay Narayan Tripathi is the Manager of Dharamshala at Hapur, U.P where accused stayed with prosecutrix on 19.11.2011. PW­5 C P Saraswat is the Manager of Dharamshala at Mathura, U.P. PW­6 Uma Kant Sharma is the owner of the hotel at Fetehpuri, Delhi. PW­7 Ms. Shikha Verma is the doctor who examined the prosecutrix and has proved the MLC of the   prosecutrix   as   Ex.PW7/A.   PW­9   Inspector   Dhara   Mishra conducted the inquiry while she was posted in CAW Cell, Dwarka. PW­10 Constable Anil Dutt is a formal witness who has proved the seizure memo as Ex.PW10/A. PW­11 is W HC Urmila who had taken the prosecutrix to the hospital for her medical examination. PW­12 Gopal Prasad Shukla is an astrologer. PW­13 SI Benketesh is the part IO of this case. PW­14 Ms. Manika, Ld. Metroplitan Magistrate has proved the statement of the prosecutrix recorded u/s 164 Cr.PC as Ex.PW1/C. PW15 WSI Chander Kanta is the investigating officer who conducted the investigation in this case.  8. Statement of accused was recorded under Section 313 Cr.P.C when a chance was given to explain the incriminating evidence against   him.   Accused   pleaded   that   he   had   travelled   with   the prosecutrix for pilgrimage on humanitarian ground. She has falsely State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 3  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. implicated him in the present case to extort money. He did not examine any witness in his defence. 9. I have heard Ms. Satwinder Kaur, Ld. APP for the State and Sh. V. K. Sharma, Ld. Counsel for the accused. I have also perused the entire material on record.  10. Ld.   Counsel   for   the   accused   has   contended   that prosecutrix has made several improvements and contradictions in her testimony before the Court. The accused is aged about 58 years and he belongs to a respectable family.   He has two married sons. The prosecutrix,   aged   about   48   years,   is   habitual   of   lodging   false complaints against different persons to extort money. She even lodged an FIR against her own nephew but, later on, the same was got quashed by her.  According to him, accused is liable to be acquitted in the present case. 11. On the other hand, Ld. APP has contended that the prosecution has proved its case against the accused beyond reasonable doubt.  12. The material witness in this case is PW1 on whose testimony the prosecution case rests. PW1 has testified that in March 2011, she was going from Delhi to Muradabad in a train. She met accused in the train and they became acquainted with each other.  On the invitation of the accused, she attended the marriage of his son at Tivoli Garden, Delhi on 26.11.2011.   In February 2012, accused asked her to accompany him to Mathura. On 03.03.2012 she along with accused went to Mathura and they stayed in the same room in a State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 4  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. guest house (name withheld). The accused, a widower, convinced her that he wanted to marry her. He kissed her on her forehead. On 04.03.2012 they went to Bankey Bihari Temple, Mathura, U. P. where accused put a garland around her neck and told her that now they were husband and wife. She has further deposed that in April 2012 on the asking of the accused she came to Delhi. She took the accused to her the evening. They stayed in a hotel at Rishikesh where accused committed rape upon her.  She stayed with the accused in the same room at hotel during her entire journey for ten days where she was On   scanning   the   various   statements   given   by   the prosecutix at various stages of investigation and trial, it reveals that she is not consistent in her version. Admitted position is that both the prosecutrix and the accused were well acquainted with each other State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 10  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. before the incident and have friendly relations. The prosecutrix has stated in her complaint­Ex.PW1/A, on which the present FIR was lodged, that she was raped by the accused for the first time in April 2012. However, she has not stated in the said complaint the date, time and place of alleged incident of rape in April 2012. She has not stated anything about the alleged incident of rape in April 2012 when her of rape in April 2012. It is a material contradiction which goes to the root of the case.   The prosecution has failed to prove beyond reasonable doubt if at the time of first encounter in April 2012 the prosecutrix was raped 'forcibly' by the accused against her wishes. She did not raise any alarm at that time nor she lodged any report with the police for the forcible rape committed upon her. If the prosecutrix was not a consenting party,  there was no occasion or reason not to report the incident to the police for the heinous crime committed by the accused of having physical relations forcibly against her wishes. Even after the first alleged incident of April 2012, the prosecutrix again accompanied the accused to Char Dham Yatra for about ten days in June 2012 where the accused allegedly committed rape upon her. As per PW­1, on 12.09.2012 in Delhi (Near Old Delhi Railway Station), on 19.11.2012 at Garhganga, on 29.11.2012 at Rudrapur, Uttarakhand in February 2013 in Delhi (Near Old Delhi Railway Station) and in April 2013 at Gandhi Nagar, Delhi the accused continued to have forcible sexual intercourse with her. The places of incidents of the State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 11  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. offence on the abovesaid dates are the different hotels booked by the accused. No cogent evidence has emerged on record to show that the physical relations were established with the prosecutrix without her consent. She was mature enough to fully understand as to what was happening between the two. There is nothing in her evidence to demonstrate that she was incapable of understanding the nature and implications of the acts which she consented to. Her consent for physical relationships, if any, was an act of conscious reason. If a fully grown up lady consents to the act of sexual intercourse and continues to indulge in such activity for long, it is an act of promiscuity on her part.   As per medical evidence, the prosecutrix was medically examined on 06.10.2014 at DDU Hospital, New Delhi. No evidence of   any   external  injury  was   found   at  the   time  of   her   medical examination. PW­7 has proved the MLC as Ex.PW7/A and during her cross­examination she has admitted that the hymen of a girl could have been torn due to other reasons such as playing games etc. There is nothing on record to suggest that it was accused who forced her to have sexual intercourse with him which went on for one year. The prosecutrix is not believed to allow the accused to have physical relations repeatedly without complaining in absence of being her a consenting party. All these circumstances create a doubt in the story of the prosecution. 29. In her cross­examination, PW­1 denied having registered any FIR against anyone prior to registration of present FIR. However, when her attention was drawn to a copy of FIR No.449/14 PS Dabri State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 12  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. dated 3.3.2014 u/s 452/341/354/323/509/427/506 IPC, she admitted that the said FIR was got registered by her against her nephew. She has further admitted that she got the abovesaid FIR quashed from the High Court of Delhi. Prosecutrix was 44 years of age at the time of registration of FIR against her nephew. Thus, the prosecutrix is not a credible witness.  30.   The   stand   taken   by   the   prosecutrix   that   she   was threatened by the accused does not inspire confidence.  No complaint was lodged by the prosecutrix immediately after the alleged incidents though she had ample opportunity to lodge the complaints against the accused. From the testimony of PW­1, it appears that she voluntarily stayed with the accused and never tried to run away from the places where   she   stayed   with   him   despite   the   fact   that   she   had   the opportunity to run away from the clutches of the accused. She never raised any alarm at that time and never disclosed the incident (s) of rape to anybody.  31. The FIR in criminal case is an extremely vital and valuable piece of evidence for the purpose of corroborating the oral evidence adduced at the trial. It is well settled proposition of law that a mere delay itself cannot be a ground to disbelieve the entire case of the prosecution. The effect of delay is to be understood in the light of the plausibility of the explanation forthcoming and must depend for consideration on all the facts and circumstances of a given case. Though not referred to or relied upon, in case of Dilawar v. State of Delhi, 2007 Cri.LJ 4709,  it has been held by the Apex Court that in State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 13  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. criminal trial one of the cardinal principle for the Court is to look for plausible explanation for the delay in lodging the report. Delay sometimes   affords   opportunity   to   the   complainant   to   make deliberation upon the complaint and to make embellishment or even make fabrications. 32. There is no photograph of marriage. There is no evidence of marriage except for the statement of the prosecutrix that accused solemnized marriage with her on 04.03.2012 at Banke Bihari Mandir, Mathura, U P by putting a garland around her neck. There is no independent witness to the said incident.   Even after the alleged marriage, no physical relations were established between the accused and the prosecutrix in March 2012.  The prosecutrix has deposed that accused told her that they were/are husband and wife after putting a garland around her neck in a temple.  The accused made physical relations with prosecutrix for the first time in April 2012 as mentioned in the complaint­Ex.PW1/B. Putting a garland around the neck in a temple ipso facto does not create any relationship akin to marriage. Where was the compulsion for the prosecutrix to establish physical relations   first   without   there   being   actual   marriage   performed according to rites and ceremonies ? Though not referred to or relied upon, in judgment – Gaurav Maggo v. State, Crl. A. No.369/2014, decided by High Court of Delhi on 29.5.2015, it has been held as under : “There is nothing in her evidence to demonstrate that she was incapable of understanding the nature and implications of the act which she consented to. Her consent for physical relations (if any) State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 14  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. was an act of conscious reason. If a fully grown up lady consents to the act of sexual intercourse on a promise to marry and continues to indulge in such activity for long, it is an act of promiscuity on her part and not an act induced by misconception of fact.”  33. Though not referred to or relied upon, in judgment­ Jayanti Rani Panda v. State of W.B., 1984 Crl. Law Journal 1535 it has been held that if a grown up girl has consented to sexual intercourse with a person who held out false promise to marry her it would not amount to consenting under any misconception of fact under Section 90 IPC and sexual intercourse by the man under these circumstance would not be an offence of rape as defined in Section 375   IPC.   Though   not   referred   to   or   relied   upon,   in   similar circumstances, in judgment ­ State v. Anupam Bhardwaj, Criminal Revision P. No. 04/2017, decided on 03.01.2017, our High Court of Delhi speaking through Hon'ble Mr. Justice Vipin Sanghi has held that no offence of rape can be said to have been committed.  34. Though not referred to or relied upon, in judgment ­ Sadashiv Ramrao Hadbe v. State of Maharashtra & Anr., 2006 (10) SCC 92, the Apex Court while reiterating that in a rape case, the accused could be convicted on the sole testimony of the prosecutrix if it is capable of inspiring the confidence in the mind of the Court, put a word of caution that the Court should be extremely careful while accepting the testimony when the entire case is improbable and unlikely to have happened. This is what has been stated: “It is true that in a rape case the accused could be convicted on the sole testimony of the prosecutrix, if it is capable of inspiring confidence in the mind of the court. If State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 15  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. the version given by the prosecutrix is unsupported by any medical evidence or the whole surrounding circumstances are highly improbable and belie the case set up by the prosecutrix, the court shall not act on the solitary evidence of the prosecutrix. The courts shall be extremely careful in acepting the sole testimony of the prosecutrix when the entire case is improbable and unlikely to happen.”  35. Though not referred to or relied upon, in judgment ­ Rai Sandeep @ Deepu v. State of NCT of Delhi, (2012) 8 SCC 21, the Supreme Court commented about the quality of the sole testimony of the prosecutrix which could be made basis to convict the accused. It held:­ “In our considered opinion, the 'sterling witness' should be of a very high quality and caliber whose version should,   therefore,   be   unassailable.   The   Court considering the version of such witness should be in a position to accept it for its face value without any hesitation. To test the quality of such a witness, the status of the witness would be immaterial and what would be relevant is the truthfulness of the statement made by such a witness. What would be more relevant would be the consistency of the statement right from the starting point till the end, namely, at the time when the witness makes the initial statement and ultimately before the Court. It should be natural and consistent with the case of the prosecution qua the accused. There should not be any prevarication in the version of such a witness. The witness should be in a position to withstand the cross­ examination of any length and strenuous it may be and under no circumstance should give room for any doubt as to the factum of the occurrence, the persons involved, as well as, the sequence of it. Such a version should have co­relation with each and everyone of other supporting material such as the recoveries made, the weapons used, the manner of offence committed, the scientific evidence and   the   expert   opinion.   The   said   version   should consistently match with the version of every other State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 16  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. witness. It can even be stated that it should be akin to the test applied in the case of circumstantial evidence where there should not be any missing link in the chain of circumstances to hold the accused guilty of the offence alleged against him. Only if the version of such a witness qualifies the above test as well as all other similar such tests to be applied, it can be held that such a witness can be called as a 'sterling witness' whose version can be accepted by the Court without any corroboration and based on which the guilty can be punished. To be more precise, the version of the said witness on the core spectrum of the crime should remain intact while all other attendant materials, namely, oral, documentary and material objects should match the said version in material particulars in order to enable the Court trying the offence to rely on the core version to sieve the other supporting materials for holding the offender guilty of the charge alleged.” 36. Though not referred to or relied upon, in judgment ­ Tameezuddin @ Tammu v. State (NCT of Delhi), (2009) 15 SCC 566, the Supreme Court held : ­ “It is true that in a case of rape the evidence of the Prosecutrix must be given predominant consideration, but to hold that this evidence has to be accepted even if the story is improbable and belies logic, would be doing violence   to   the   very   principles   which   govern   the appreciation of evidence in a criminal matter.”  37. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, I am of the opinion that the prosecution has failed to prove its case against the accused beyond reasonable doubt. Hence, the accused is acquitted. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged. Documents, if any, be released to the surety/Counsel. In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., the accused is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of State vs. Surender Kumar Gupta.  Page 17  of 18 FIR No.629/14, P.S. Dabri. Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to file an appeal challenging the present judgment. Ahlmad is directed to page and bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record.  File be consigned to Record Room. Prosecution in support of its case has examined the prosecutrix as PW1.  She has deposed that she came to know accused through Facebook in year 2011 and they became friends. They used to chat with each other. In the beginning of 2015, she met accused at his office situate in Sector­7, Dwarka. Thereafter, they started meeting each other as they had likings for each other. Accused proposed to marry her. However, their respective families were not agreeable to their marriage. PW1 has further deposed that she had consensual sexual relations for the first time with the accused at his house at RZ­ 99C­1,   Street   No.4,   Khandelwal   Complex,   Palam,   New   Delhi. Thereafter, they had consensual sexual relations at the house of accused on several occasions till February, 2016. In mid of February, 2016, the family of the accused was not agreeable for marriage due to difference in their castes. Accused also started ignoring her because of pressure of his family. She has further deposed that their families were persuaded to get them married and, consequently, date 24.2.2016 was SC No. 441270/16 (State vs. Deepak Sharma) Page 2 of 4 fixed   for   their   marriage.   However,   the   marriage   could   not   be solemnized on that day as the father of the accused had sustained injuries. The mother of the accused being a superstitious lady got suspicious that her husband had received injuries due to her. On 24.2.2016 a quarrel took place over this issue. As per prosecutrix, she got annoyed and lodged the complaint Ex.PW1/A. She has proved her statement u/s.164 Cr.PC as Ex.PW1/B. PW1 has further deposed that she got married to accused on 22.4.2016 at Arya Samaj Mandir, Sector­10, Dwarka. She has proved her marriage certificate in this regard as Ex.PW1/C. PW­1 has categorically deposed that accused never had forcible sexual relations at any point of time with her. 7. Prosecutrix was declared hostile and was allowed to be cross   examined   by   the   Ld.   APP.   However,   even   after   cross­ examination at length nothing incriminating has come out in evidence against the accused. She has categorically denied the suggestion that the accused had committed forcible sexual intercourse with her on the false pretext of marriage. 8. From the testimony of PW1 it is clear that accused never raped the prosecutrix. As the prosecutrix has not supported the case of the prosecution, the examination of other witnesses was dispensed with. 9. The statement of the accused u/s.313 Cr.PC was also not recorded as there is no incriminating evidence against him. 10. Considering the facts and circumstances of this case, I am of the opinion that the prosecution has failed to prove its case against SC No. 441270/16 (State vs. Deepak Sharma) Page 3 of 4 the accused. Hence, the accused is acquitted. His personal bond is cancelled and surety is discharged. Documents, if any, be released to the surety/Counsel. In terms of Section 437(A) Cr.P.C., accused is directed to furnish personal bond in the sum of Rs.25,000/­ with one surety in the like amount for a period of six months for his appearance before the High Court of Delhi in the event the prosecution wishes to file an appeal challenging the present judgment. Ahlmad is directed to page and bookmark the file so as to enable the digitisation of the entire record. File be consigned to Record Room. However, accused Rahul, present in court today (correctly identified), was present in said house and he used to administer 'Ganja' and some tablets to me and after consuming the same, I used to remain in intoxicated state. Thereafter, accused used to call some persons there who used to do sex with me against my consent. Accused Rahul was indulged into sex racket. As I always used to remain under the influence of the drugs given to me by accused Rahul, I do not know the dates when the said persons used to commit forcible sexual intercourse with me who were used to be called by accused Rahul for the said purpose. Accused never used to pay me anything, however, on one occasion when I had fallen sick, accused Rahul had given me Rs.2,000/-.  After some time, I was taken to a flat situated near Metro Pillar No.753 near Dwarka More, by accused Rahul. In the said flat also, accused Rahul used to call his   clients   who   used   to   commit   forcible   sexual intercourse with me. In this flat, some quarrel had taken place between accused Rahul and one of the clients who had come to have sexual intercourse with me at the behest of accused Rahul as accused Rahul had taken his gold chain and purse etc. Thereafter, I was taken to some house at Munirka by brother of accused Rahul namely Siddharth as after the said Judgment 12 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors incident of quarrel, accused Rahul had run away from there. In the said flat at Munirka, Siddharth ……  had also committed forcible sexual intercourse with me. Thereafter, he had gone somewhere after locking me inside the room. Siddharth had also threatened me to kill before leaving the said room so I did not raise any alarm. The said room in which I was raped by Siddharth was not belonging to him and it was the room of some other persons. The lock of the said room was opened by the occupants of the room. They did not know that I was inside the room. On finding an opportunity, I ran away from the said room and reached P.S. Munirka. However, in P.S. Munirka, my complaint was not lodged as I was told that the incident had taken place in the jurisdiction of P.S. Bindapur. So I reached P.S. Bindapur and lodged the complaint. Accused Abhijeet Kumar and accused Sandeep   Singh   @   Shooter………   used   to   bring various clients at the flat situated near Metro Pillar No.753,   who   used   to   commit   forcible   sexual intercourse with me.  There were two rooms near Metro Pillar no.753 where accused Abhijeet Kumar and accused Sandeep Singh @ Shooter used to bring various clients who used to commit forcible sexual intercourse upon me and accused Rahul used to take money from the said clients for the said purpose. Accused Rahul had also committed forcible sexual intercourse upon me several times in the said room of the flat situated near Metro Pillar No.753. Accused Rahul had committed forcible sexual intercourse with me in the said room in the beginning of this year, however, I do not recollect the dates as I am not much literate   and   also   because   I   used   to   remain   in intoxicated state due to drugs administered to me by accused Rahul. There were some other girls also in Judgment 13 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors the said flat near Metro Pillar No.753 who were also kept forcibly by accused Rahul and they were also forced to indulge into sexual acts by various clients by accused Rahul. I had told accused Rahul several times that I do not want to indulge into such forcible sexual acts. However, I was beaten by accused Rahul and he used to force me to have forcible sexual acts with himself and various clients.   After arrest of accused Siddharth prosecutrix deposed as under: Accused Siddharth and Rahul used to administer drugs on me forcibly and if I used to refuse then they used to cut my forehand with a blade and then administer drugs to me. I received various cut injuries on my forearm.  Witness at this stage shows her forearm on which cut injuries are visible. Some cut injuries are also visible on her neck. In respect of her cut injuries on neck, witness states that once she tried to escape from the captivity then accused Rahul inflicted   injuries   on   her   neck   by   a   blade   and threatened to kill her in case she would try to escape. 18.  First argument of the defence is that testimony of prosecutrix is wavering and she has changed her versions in different stages of trial, which renders her testimony not worthy of any credence. In order to examine the veracity of testimony of prosecutrix, it would be appropriate to scrutinize as to what she has alleged.  Judgment 14 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 19.  Allegations appearing against accused Rahul: In her complaint Ex. PW1/A, prosecutrix stated that about two months prior to of lodging complaint accused Rahul established physical relations with her after intoxicating her by administering a cold drink mixed with a tablet and thereafter many times after mixing an intoxicating tablet in her food accused established physical relations with her and for the last time, Rahul raped her in January when there was nobody else in the flat.  20.  In her statement  Ex. PW1/B, prosecutrix did not narrate any incident rather alleged that accused Rahul used to keep her intoxicated and has raped her.  21.  In her examination-in-chief prosecutrix deposed that accused   Rahul   committed   forcible   sexual   intercourse upon her several times in flat situated near  Metro Pillar No. 753.   Judgment 15 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors she   testified   that   accused   Rahul   committed   forcible   sexual intercourse with her and she used to remain in intoxicated state due to drugs administered to her by accused Rahul.  22.   Prosecutrix during her cross-examination deposed that accused Rahul used to administer 'Ganja' and some tablets to her and after consuming the same, she used to remain in intoxicated state. Though prosecutrix in her complaint Ex. PW1/A made a specific allegation that accused established physical relations with her, after administering intoxicating tablets in a cold drink. However, this allegation of prosecutrix is not appearing in her subsequent statement Ex. PW1/B nor in her testimony. It is noteworthy that in her deposition for first time prosecutrix stated about administering of ganja to her by accused Rahul. None of her previous statements mentions about ganja being administered to her rather in her versions prosecutrix maintained that accused was mixing intoxicating substance in her cold drink and food. Judgment 16 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 23.  Prosecutrix testified that while she was working as a maid in Rajouri Garden, from there her aunt took her to a house at unknown address and location. Accused Rahul was present in the house and used to administer  ganja  to her. During her cross- examination prosecutrix maintained that she was administered intoxicating substance which has diluted her memory. However, it is evident that prosecutrix did not disclose as to how she came in contact with accused Rahul or where is that Aunt who introduced prosecutrix to accused. That lady is not even cited in the present case nor her particulars are forthcoming so to find out that under what circumstances prosecutrix was left at the house of accused. 24.  Prosecutrix further testified that she does not know about family members of accused Rahul and accused never spoke to any of his family members in her presence but in the same breadth prosecutrix testified that accused took her to the place where his wife and daughter was staying. She deposed that under intoxicated state accused Rahul took her photographs with his wife Judgment 17 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors and daughter. Testimony of prosecutrix goes to show that she was well acquainted with family of accused Rahul and her denial in this regard is found to be false.  25.  Nonetheless, prosecutrix admits that she was taken to a nearby market by accused Abhijit and Shooter to buy clothes and she purchased a jeans top from a shop. Prosecutrix did not raise any alarm in the market nor made a complaint to the shopkeeper that she was kept under confinement by the accused persons or was forced to do prostitution. Conduct of prosecutrix shows that she was freely roaming with accused persons in a market and despite having opportunity to escape or raise an alarm, she did not do so.   26.  Prosecutrix admitted having spoken to her mother from mobile phone of accused Rahul. Prosecutrix admits that she did not  inform her mother that she was forced to indulge in sexual act by accused Rahul. Though prosecutrix explained that she was   Judgment 18 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors threatened by accused Rahul to kill her if she disclosed the said fact to her but fact remains that prosecutrix did talk to her mother. Prosecutrix could have disclosed her ordeal to her mother in her local lingo if not otherwise. Prosecutrix was residing alone in Delhi for three years without family support and she is expected to have an understanding to give at-least a hint to her mother of her captivity but for reasons best known to prosecutrix she did not tell her mother anything.  27.  In her statement, Ex. PW1/A prosecutrix mentions that on 18/19.02.2016 a customer misbehaved with Natasha, then all of them gave beatings to customer, snatched his money, mobile, purse and chain. In the commotion somebody called police and Rahul signaled all of them to run away. Her statement makes it evident that she was part of association and on signal of accused she along with her associates ran way.  Judgment 19 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 28.  It is evident that prosecutrix at that point of time did not wait for police to arrive to disclose her ordeal to police rather chose to accompany accused persons to reach Munirka in Taxi with accused Siddharth. More so, having every opportunity to escape prosecutrix did not escape nor did she report the incident to police but instead she preferred to remain with accused persons and ran away from the spot. 29.  Allegations against accused Siddarth: Prosecutrix further gives details of said incident by stating that she stayed at Munirka for 3 days with Sidharth and Abhijeet and 4-5 other boys, with whom she was not acquainted and she had no complaint against them. In her statement  Ex. PW1/B  (recorded U/s 164 Cr.P.C) prosecutrix does not say anything against accused Siddarth except that he confined and threatened her.  30.  In her deposition prosecutrix alleged that accused Siddarth committed forcible sexual relations with her in a flat at Judgment 20 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors Munirka but as stated above this assertion of prosecutrix that accused Sidharth committed sexual assault on her is not appearing in any of her previous statements. Deposition of prosecutrix is entirely different to her complaint where she did not make any allegation against accused Siddarth rather stated that she has no complaints against him.    31.  There is one another aspect of the matter i.e. a case FIR No. 165/16 PS Bindapur was registered U/s 394/34 IPC against accused persons as per the FIR (Ex. DW1/A). DW1 SI Mukesh Kumar is investigating officer of that case and he specifically deposed that during investigation of the case, name of prosecutrix cropped up and she was also interrogated in this FIR. DW1 deposed that in the disclosure statement of Shivani @ Jassi, it was stated that prosecutrix was residing in the same house where other accused persons were residing. As per prosecutrix in the intervening night of 18- 19.02.2016, there was a scuffle between accused Rahul and a customer who misbehaved with one girl Judgment 21 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors Natasha and thereafter that customer was beaten, his belongings were snatched and he was thrown out. Other persons who were with prosecutrix were named as an accused in that case and prosecutrix escaped from there. Prosecutrix did not come forward to disclose about her confinement rather she chose to ran away with other accused persons. This conduct of prosecutrix shows that she was under apprehension that she might be named as an accused in case FIR no. 165/16 (Ex. DW1/A) and for this reason she escaped from the spot. Therefore, the defence has rightly pointed out that allegations leveled by prosecutrix in this case were due to the fact that the prosecutrix wanted to wriggle out of the allegations against her in said FIR.  32.  Allegations under Immoral Traffic Act: Prosecutrix in all her statements alleged that accused Rahul was running a sex racket with his aides Abhijit Kumar @ Tarzan and Sandeep Singh @ Shooter. As per her Abhijit Kumar @ Tarzan and Sandeep Singh @ Shooter used to bring customers and she was forced to Judgment 22 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors oblige them in a flat at second floor, Dwarka Mor, Near Nawada Metro Pillar no.753 which was run as brothel.    33.  No investigation has been conducted from neighbors where allegedly the 'brothel' was being run. Nothing has come on record if any neighbor residing nearby suspected objectionable or illegal activities going on in the tenanted premises. No such complaint was ever lodged by any resident of locality with police.  34.  Call Details Records of accused persons are not collected nor scrutinized to find out details of alleged customers or clients visiting flat. Prosecutrix in her initial statement Ex PW1/A specifically stated that on 18/19.02.2016 a customer had a scuffle with accused persons but in present case, he has not been cited as witness nor examined by prosecution. Prosecutrix also mentioned about presence of 2-3 girls but none of them are part of investigations. Nonetheless, prosecutrix did not explain as to why she preferred to stay with accused persons after coming to know Judgment 23 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors that they are engaged in sex trade. Despite having opportunity, prosecutrix preferred to stay with them. Apparently, prosecutrix was a willing and consenting party in the entire episode. Her statement cannot be taken on its face value to base conviction of accused persons without independent corroboration which is lacking in the instant case. Nonetheless, there is no evidence on record to suggest that accused  Abhijit Kumar @ Tarzan and Sandeep Singh @ Shooter used to bring customers for prosecutrix or other girls residing in that house.  35.  In  'Sadashiv   Ramrao   Hadbe   vs.   State   of Maharashtra & Anr.' 2006 (10) SCC 92, Apex Court while reiterating that in a rape case, accused could be convicted on sole testimony of the prosecutrix if it is capable of inspiring the confidence in the mind of the Court, put a word of caution that the Court should be extremely careful while accepting the testimony when entire case is improbable and unlikely to have happened.  Judgment 24 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors "It is true that in a rape case the accused could be convicted on the sole testimony of the prosecutrix, if it is capable of inspiring confidence in the mind of the court. If the version given by the prosecutrix is unsupported by any medical evidence or the 'whole surrounding circumstances are highly improbable and belie the case set; up by the prosecutrix, the court shall   not   act   on   the   solitary   evidence   of   the prosecutrix. The courts shall be extremely careful in accepting the sole testimony of the prosecutrix when the entire case is improbable and unlikely to happen." 36.  In 'Abbas Ahmed Choudhury v. State of Assam', (2010) 12 SCC 115, observing that a case of sexual assault has to be proved beyond reasonable doubt as any other case and that there is no presumption that a prosecutrix would always tell the entire story truthfully, the Hon'ble Supreme Court held : "Though the statement of prosecutrix must be given prime consideration, at the same time, broad principle that the prosecution has to prove its case beyond reasonable doubt applies equally to a case of rape and there could be no presumption that a prosecutrix would always tell the entire story truthfully. In the instant case, not only the testimony of the victim woman   is   highly   disputed   and   unreliable,   her testimony has been thoroughly demolished by the deposition of DW-1." Judgment 25 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 37.  Hon'ble Supreme Court in the decision reported as (2012) 7 SCC 171 'Narender Kumar Vs. State (NGT of Delhi)' held : "23. The courts while trying an accused on the charge of rape, must deal with the case with utmost sensitivity, examining the broader probabilities of a case and not get swayed by minor contradictions or insignificant discrepancies in the evidence of the witnesses which are not of a substantial character. However, even in a case of rape, the onus is always on the prosecution to prove, affirmatively each ingredient of the offence it seeks to establish and such onus never shifts. It is no part of the duty of the defence to explain as to how and why in a rape case the victim and other witnesses have falsely implicated the accused. The prosecution case has to stand on its own legs and cannot take support from the weakness of the case of defence. However great the suspicion against the accused and however strong the moral belief and conviction of the court, unless the offence of the accused is established beyond reasonable doubt on the basis of legal evidence and material on the record, he cannot be convicted for an offence. There is an initial presumption of innocence of the accused and the prosecution has to bring home the offence against the accused by reliable evidence. The accused is entitled to   the   benefit   of   every   reasonable   doubt.   (Vide Tukaram Vs. State of Maharashtra (1979) 2 SCC 143 and Uday Vs.. State of Karnataka 2003 II AD (S.C.) 358) Judgment 26 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 24. The prosecution has to prove its case beyond reasonable doubt and cannot take support from the weakness of the case of defence. There must be proper legal evidence and material on record to record the conviction of the accused. The conviction can be based on sole testimony of the prosecutrix provided it lends assurance of her testimony. However, in case the court has reason not to accept the version of the prosecutrix on its face value, it may look for corroboration. In case the evidence is read in its totality and the story projected by the prosecutrix is found to be improbable, the prosecutrix's case becomes liable to be rejected." 38.   It is evident that at every stage of trial prosecutrix has come up with a new version which is hardly consistent with her previous versions. It is clear from the evidence that prosecutrix is not telling the truth. Deposition of prosecutrix cannot be treated as trustworthy and reliable.  As narrated above testimony of prosecutrix is wavering and she has given different versions of the incident.   Testimony   of   prosecutrix   suffers   from   material inconsistencies   (improvements)   and   thus   is  unreliable   and unworthy of credence. Judgment 27 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 39.    Allegations against accused Siddarth U/s 174-A IPC: As far as charge for offence U/s 174-A IPC is concerned, it is matter of record that accused Siddarth was declared proclaimed offender. However, offence U/s 174-A IPC is a distinct offence which is triable by the Magistrate. No separate report was filed U/s 173 Cr.P.C. in relation to this offence. 40.  It has been held by the Hon'ble High Court of Delhi in Crl. A. 391/2013 in case Mohd. Jamal @ Ranjha Vs. State that offence U/s 174-A IPC is to be tried by the Court of Metropolitan Magistrate and it is the Court of Metropolitan Magistrate who is entitled to take cognizance of the said offence. Accordingly, the accused cannot be convicted  U/s 174-A IPC by this Court.  Judgment 28 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 41.  From above stated discussions it emerges that : i) Testimony of prosecutrix is inconsistent with her previous statements and is not found trustworthy. ii) Prosecutrix had every opportunity to raise an alarm in market, she could have informed her mother about her confinement or on 18/19.02.2016 could have escaped or informed police but she preferred to stay with accused persons. iii) Testimony of prosecutrix is inconsistent and material improvement to her earlier statements as to her sexual assault by accused Siddarth.   iv) There is no evidence to substantiate allegations under Immoral Traffic Act. v) Prosecutrix was herself a suspect in case  FIR No. 165/16 PS Bindapur as per which a person was robbed by accused persons and their associates. vi) Allegations U/s 174-A IPC against accused Siddharth are not proved.  42.  Conclusion:  In the light of above discussions, it is held that prosecution has failed to bring on record clear, cogent and consistent evidence against accused persons. Hence, by giving benefit of doubt, accused persons are acquitted of the offence they are charged with.  Judgment 29 of 30  SC No: 441232/16 State Vs. Rahul & Ors 43.  Surety of accused  Abhijit Kumar @ Tarzan and Sandeep Singh @ Shooter are discharged. Their bail bond stands canceled.  Accused persons are directed to furnish a personal & surety bond in sum of Rs. 10,000/- each under Section 437-A Cr.P.C which shall remain in force for period of six months. Accused Rahul, Siddarth and  Abhijit Kumar @ Tarzan  are in judicial custody. They be released from jail, if not required in any other case. Sessions Judge (SFTC)    South-West, Dwarka Courts, Delhi Judgment 30 of 30
